It is certainly better than the DC deck-builder.

RATING: 7.5
I had high hopes for this game, and after four plays it has been a bit of a disappointment.  There has been a lot of talk about how the game is too easy when played strictly as a coop game, and I must disagree with that.  Of my four games, three have ended in a loss for all the players (well, 2 were losses, one was a "tie" with the villain deck being exhausted before the Mastermind could be defeated).  I would think the players in my gaming group are pretty good at deckbuilders as we play them fairly regularly, so I don't feel like we're playing poorly.  I think instead the issue is that there is high variability in the difficulty of the game based on a number of factors: the Mastermind, the Scheme, the Villain deck composition, and the Hero deck composition.  This makes it very hard to estimate the difficulty of a particular game setup.

Now, all that is not to say that I dislike that the game is hard.  I don't mind losing at coop games.  However, I don't feel like this game works as a pure coop because there is very little player interaction.  There is very little players can do to help the other players.  It feels a lot like multiplayer solitaire - coop style.  And after those first four games, that doesn't feel like a very good way to make a coop game.

Having said all that, I'm still rating this one as a 7, though that is liable to change with further plays.  Right now, though, I can't say whether I expect it will go up or down.

UPDATE (1-5-13): I got in two more plays of the game (both at 5 players, both saw the mastermind defeated), and for the first time we decided to count points after defeating the mastermind.  I feel like this did add a bit more excitement to the game.  I feel this game is lacking when played as a pure coop because there's not much players can do to assist each other and there's not much discussion to be had about strategy.  When played semi-cooperatively, I think it becomes a bit more interesting.  Overall, I still think the game is good, but not great.

UPDATE (11-6-13): After a year, an expansion and numerous plays, the game has earned a bit of a bump in the rating and a move up my [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/geeklist/143773/admiralacfs-game-rankings]game ranking geeklist[/url].  All of my previous comments still apply, I've simply come to enjoy it a bit more.  It's a fun game and I like bringing it out every so often.

+Excellent artwork.
+The board is very well done and adds a lot to the gameplay.
+The card effects are nicely thematic.
+Lots of variation in setups makes from lots of replayability.

=Doesn't work well as an entirely cooperative game.
=High variability in difficulty level.
=Numerous reused card images (this can be helpful in cleaning up the game).

-The deck-building system requires some thematic abstraction.
-Limited card buying options reduces strategic depth.
-Setup and tear down time is long compared to the time it takes to play.
-Dividers are unlabelled.

RATING: 7
I played this game just once, so these are mostly impressions that may change after multiple plays.

Legendary Marvel never caught my interest, maybe due to the fact that I'm not a big fan of either deck-building games or superheroes. Also, even if I'm not usually a theme guy, the mechanisms of this game and its theme seem like they couldn't be more disconnected and that further reduced my interest in the game. Now that I tried it, I can definitively say that my second impression was true: there's really no theme here. Yet I was surprised to see how much I enjoyed this game.

On the plus side Legendary Marvel is a game with rules that are pretty fast to explain and mechanisms that are easy to grasp. Like Dominion, it's also a game all about deck-optimization and combo-building and a lot of satisfaction can come out of that. On the other hand Legendary doesn't really feel like a cooperative game. Sure you have common objectives, but there's really not a lot you can do to help your teammates. Many times all the cooperation you are capable of is to leave a card for another player to buy or let someone else defeat a particular enemy.

Yet I find this game enjoyable. It flows smoothly, turns come back quickly, the game doesn't take too long and it's satisfactory to personalize your strategy to overcome the challenges that the villain shoots at you. Furthermore you get a lot of variety and re-play value just with the base game and there's a lot of expansions that can add to that. I still might not love this game nor its theme, but Marvel Legendary was a pleasant surprise for me. I would gladly try it again in the future. Thumbs up!

RATING: 7
It is a good game, with, of course, a Marvel superhero theme well explored in the deckbuilding mechanics. Well, it uses a similar deckbuilding mechanic than Star Realms with cards combining with each other by symbols activating even better powers and I enjoy that.

What I didn't enjoy, and prefer Sentinels of the Multiverse than this, is that you actualy don't play with one superhero, you play with the combination of them in your own hand, playing solo may make this feel better as you control all the heroes and it is ok. But with more people I prefer each one controlling a superhero and, combining one with each other, beating the supervillain and the scenario, and this, Sentinels of Multiverse does in a much better way than Legendary.

RATING: 10
Best deck building game IMO. All others that I have played end up becoming combo fests where no one really cares what others are doing and they are just racing to see who can get to finish line.

Legendary forces you to interact as a team which adds a great dynamic. You are helping each other as well as hindering each other depending on the time of the game. Perfect twist to the deck building genre that in my mind was getting very stale.

Also love a lot of the flavor, but I do admit some is random or forced.

Set up time is the only real fault of this game and once you are experienced it shouldnt be difficult at all.

RATING: 7.5
My rating for Legendary has really fluctuated over time. I'd give my first experience (base game, 2 player) a 5, but with expansions and/or 3 or 4 players, it's a much better experience. 

Setup/put away time is still a major issue that keeps it from getting to the table more often.  

Luck can also be a factor with some schemes, but not really much different than getting a run of good or bad draws in pandemic.

Where the game really shines is in theme.  The mechanisms are tied well to the theme, and if you like Marvel, this is a good game, but only after adding one or more expansions (unless you like easy co ops)

RATING: 10
I absolutely LOVE this game. This ranking includes the rating with several expansions. I have really gotten into deck builders of late and this is the best. The amount of variety from the types of heros you can add to you deck(each hero plays completely different) to the villain decks, masterminds and schemes all combining for different experiences really makes this a fast playing, infinitely replay-able experience. The game does require some organizational skill on your part to help with set up. I also highly recommend the app that lets you randomize scenarios. Most important expansion is definitely Dark City. I also love the Villains box though this one certainly complicates the game quite a bit. Who doesnt want to play as Magneto, Venom and Ultron?

RATING: 6
Es un juego entretenido pero analizando las partidas que he jugado le veo algunos puntos negativos:

- El setup puede ser muy farragoso

- No veo demasiada personalización de superhéroes. Sí, hay muchas cartas de ellos, pero al final son un poco todas lo mismo, comprar o atacar con algunos matices... además, cada jugador puede tener cartas de todos los superhéroes a la vez... eso particularmente me disgusta pq la gracia estaría en llevar cada uno a varios con exclusividad sobre sus poderes y habilidades.

- Si te gustan los comics las ilustraciones del juego te parecerán un poco flojas y además algunas se repiten mucho (las del juego básico).

En la parte buena:

- El juego es rápido y divertido. Partidas de 45 minutos.

- Para varios jugadores funciona bien (pero 3 máximo, pq con más puede resultar muy lento)

- Pese a su mecánica simple, la gran cantidad de cartas le da cierta variabilidad para que no resulte repetitivo.

RATING: 7
3/21/16: Rating is based upon initial play.  Rating may go up with additional plays.

A semi-cooperative game.  Takes the deck building mechanics found in Ascension and Star Realms and builds on them. You start with low level fighters and recruiters and build up your deck.  It has a nice theme and the good artwork.  The characters are the Marvel Heroes that I grew up with.  You fight the bad guys and build up strength to fight the mastermind.

Has a nicely laid out board, and the insert is built so that it can handle sleeves and expansions.  

Plays well with 3 or 4.  Have not tried with 2.  There is a solitaire version available.

RATING: 9
This is a really fantastic game that I rate highly largely due to the variety you get game-to-game. With expansions that just gets bigger and bigger. My only complaint, and it isn't even such a bad thing, is that it can sometimes be frustratingly difficult. There are some villains that are just incredibly challenging, and require masterful coordination and/or the perfect hero set up to defeat. I consider myself and my play group very experienced board gamers, but we have gone many games in a row getting defeated by the same villain, until we finally are forced to pick "only the best" heroes in order to defeat the boss.

As I say, this isn't that much of a problem. Challenge is necessary for co-op games, but I do feel certain cards could have been balanced better to make them more strategically viable against some of the tougher villains.

RATING: 7.5
Bought by a friend, Legendary is a deck building game by Upper Deck. Players have the ability to recruit heroes into their deck by utilizing recruit points and fighting points to combat villains. The game comes with different schemes and different masterminds to vary the game. Each scenario is unique with different henchmen, villain groups, and heroes that can be recruited for the fight. I find that the game is pretty fun with the right company. There are even variants that allow for variability, and the game also scales according to the number of players. Certain situations require more thought-out plans, but one thing is certain, you must defeat the mastermind at least 4 times to call yourself victorious. The setup can be quite time consuming at first, but this game is definitely fun to play.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4.4
Initial rating, based on a single (extremely frustrating) 5-player game, in which both the scheme and the mastermind required the same type of heroes, of which there were very few in the game, our HQ was stuffed right from the beginning with super expensive heroes, most of the enemies were too tough, and we'd each picked up 4-5 wounds before the game had gotten properly under way. Rating probably will go up a bit with further plays, assuming those will be less unbalanced, but that the game allows for this level of imbalance means I'll never rate it very high. I don't care too much for the superhero theme either, and in general I suspect I'll consider this a flawed copy of Ascension, with particularly the very small market being an extremely limiting factor, making luck play far too large a role.

RATING: 5
A fairly well executed deck drafting game that ultimately fails for me in terms of scalability and tension. In all my games, I've never felt worried about the outcome of the game. Because of the lack of tension in playing against the plot, the semi-cooperative element seems to be the only weak driving tension in the game. There's also an illusion of replayability because of the shear number of heroes in the base game. Aside from mixing things up with the heroes and villains (and even then), the games feel fairly similar: start slow, be patient, build up your deck and then kill everything in sight with ease. 

While the theme is extremely attractive, ultimately the game play doesn't hold enough interest to make this a keeper.

Played with 5 people and thought that the game ended too fast, we barely had any turns to really develop our decks and build combos (and see them show up).
The theme may not be mechanically strong, but with all the artwork and the vibrant colours the whole Superhero thing is there. And it helps to grasp the game because you're most likely familiar with most of the heroes (unlike in Dominion where the name of the card and its effect only have a very loose connection, it any)

The semi-coop, the whole "Everyone won, but X is the better winner" just doesn't work for me (and probably never will).
We had a chat about that semi-coop after our play and I was told that there are only so few cards that really build on the coop-idea.
Furthermore there was no need to help each other as the villain had "Difficulty: Walk in the park".
So all in all, coop feels really like an after-thought was was quickly tacked on.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

ashley played
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
(Update: 1st multiplayer session - 2P)
Losing faith in this games ability to reach the heights that I've experienced with Knizia's LotR. Really want to try this with a larger, more enthusiastic group to see if it can redeem itself, but I really have my doubts about whether this game can have a good interactive flow and escape the mechanical feeling I had this game. Positive about this play through is that the game felt easy and light, welcoming almost (a plus as a gateway game) didnt overstay its welcome and had a theme that was waiting to be embraced. So not a complete loss, but a more limited audience than I was hoping for upon acquisition. 

(Initial Rating: Based in two two-player solitaire games):
Definitely feels lighter than the average deck-builder which might be good or bad. Good for non-gamers. Boring for the average gamer.

+1.0 points for theme and the scenarios, enjoyed the setup and how they played out mechanically.

I will say that the complaint I read about where players can opt to keep building up their deck rather than attack the Mastermind causing the game to drag on for way, way, way too long particularly for a game that's so light.  In certain scenarios there should almost be a mandatory rule that if a player has enough power to attack the Mastermind, they must attack him. I could see it thematically as the Mastermind, themselves, learning of all this power the heroes have accumulated and confronting them, only to be rebuffed.

In my second game, I squandered a chance to defeat the Mastermind "mid-game" resulting in my decks becoming clogged with "recruiting" cards that prevented me from attacking at full power resulting in a long drawn out "escape" of the bad guys. A scenario that would be embarrassingly painful to me with the groups I normally play with: non-gamers that are still being convinced that games are short and fun, along with gamers that have little patience for overly light games that last for two hours.

However, I do hold out hope for this game and will cautiously try it with my game groups because of how the first game I tried played out.  

The general synopsis of the game was that Magneto's master strikes were well countered by the three X-men in the hero deck, but the team struggled throughout because of the tech required to counter the the wounds inflicted by the Legacy Virus which also acted as a countdown to Evil's victory This lack of tech was personified by Black Widow's cards. That's it. 

The way it played out, one deck ran lots of attack and strength cards taking a lot of wounds, crushing the other deck (42-21) as well as the Mastermind (3-1). But what really made it a standout game was that the "winning" deck couldnt have done it with the second deck running the "wimpy" Widow that happened to have the only power (tech) that could slow Evil down long enough for Good to actually win.

So even though, technically, it was a slaughter, it was actually a "team victory. It just depends on how you look at it.

And in closing, I have to say that I enjoy the characters that now and than whack their "friends." I've read a lot of complaints about it but that's actually a huge plus in my book, right along with the classification of this game as "semi-cooperative." Lots of the guys and gals have huge egos or darkness in them, not to mention some mental or emotional instability. On the surface it can be annoying at the least and dangerous at the worst, but at the end of the day it's who these character are and sometimes it's the reason they are so powerful in the first place. Or like the Hulk, they both come from places so intertwined that there is no way to separate the two. This game would be painfully bland without Deadpool screwing with everyone or the Hulk smashing everyone and everything, now and then.

RATING: 9
I love super heros, I love cooperative games, and I love deck-building in Dominion!  So this game should have been a homerun! Plus it's got the Marvel license so it includes my favorite characters. Yet somehow my first plays just didn't completely grab me. For one thing I really don't like the solo-win style of cooperative game. I want to fully work together, but we have to compete. My other big problem is the way you draft cards to your deck. With Dominion I know what's available, so I can buy early planning out my later strategy based on the other things that are available. Here you buy a card from the five face-up and hope later you find others that work well with the early ones you bought. Not to mention the fact that you have to just try and remember what the actions were on the early cards you bought. Yet it still has some neat stuff going on. I liked the thematic connection some of the cards made, and the variety of the villains/schemes you will face is nice. I'm not abandoning the game yet, but I wish it had just a little bit more fun to it.

RATING: 6
The game play is fun, addictive, easy to learn, and fast.  I recommend it for the game play.

However, it doesn't have the replay value, customization,  or depth of strategy that Dominion has.  Since Dominion is the original deck builder game, it is the standard against which all other deck builders will be measured.  Legendary falls short.

Also, it seems Upper Deck has production issues.  Some of the card backs are not uniform, some are bluer than others.  The cards themselves don't seem sturdy enough to stand up to the rigors of repeated shuffling.  And for goodness sake, why can't they help with the organizing?!  The cards fall everywhere.  Borrow a tip from Dominion and have a place for all the different segregated card types.  Yes, they give you dividers, but they are unlabeled and just fall loose like everything else.  You need to add your own means of spacing, organizing, and protecting your cards.  As a result, it takes a solid 10 minutes minimum to set up a game and another 5 minimum to strike it afterwards.  If it weren't for these issues, I'd probably rate it a 9.

It's worth playing a few times, but ownership is a maybe.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Why 7.... Can be a 8-9 if you want a verses game rather then Co-op game.
Does not work well has co-op.

So many cards.... you will have to find a system to store them. Core box is okay, once you start adding the expansions, you will find you have to set up your own storage system. I use index cards and it works great, all the cards are in two boxes.But sooo many cards...

Enjoyable game, will take a few plays to understand completely. It is not complex, but there are many things that are altered with certian skills the cards have. Like Phasing and Teleport, and all the dozens of little symbols mean. But once it clicks it sticks.

So many options, but really they are all the same. Draw cards til you or the game wins. There is much more there but there is so many random things, and was to set up that the core is what is the same every time and that core is draw cards for game and you, winner is the one that is luckiest draw,

Few issues, you're on same team, but you're also not on the same team? It is like they were not sure if it was a co-op game, or a verse game... so they made it both and it does not work as either. You lose the game because you can not help a player beat an enemy even if you have the card they require in your hand. So the whole team loses because you can ot help the others. Only real way to help others is not take cards they want, or ask if they have a card in hand before attacking someone that will require that card.

Legendary is great fun to play, and this is the one the family always plays, they do really like the game. These bad elements mostly are listed because if you can look past these then you will love game. IF you do not care for the theme, then maybe pick up Alien version has this is my favourite of the set and works much better game play wise. Just seems the family prefers marvel for its setting, so it is what is played more times then not.

RATING: 8
Legendary is more fun that is has a right to be. The deckbuilding isn't that sophisticated. The theme is not integrated quite as well as I'd like...but it strangely works. It helps to have a buddy playing who is into the universe, of course. The game just slides along so smoothly, there is just too little downtime to gripe. The little combos are fun; the different personalities of the different superheroes are fun; hitting the super villain hard is fun. The game is just...pleasant fun... in a way that games with more gravitas and ambition sometimes just aren't. I think buying the Dark City expansion is obligatory; it seems to kill pretty effectively the semi-co-op element of the game which the base set has that never worked for me (and others). Recommended - with the Dark City expansion.

RATING: 6.5
Decent co-op/competitive evolution of Dominion. Great theme and artwork to the cards, and everything fits together well. However, absolutely nothing felt fresh about this game- all the mechanics we've seen in other games and implemented in a more original manner. 

On top of that, unlike Dominion there is a far greater amount of cards being removed from your hand as a result of game effects (heroes being 'Feasted' on, etc.). This  lead, for me, to a much more frustrating injection of luck than other similar deck building games. Multiple times early on in the game I had my best card which I had just bought and never used, be the top card that got "KO'ed" and out of my deck. I then was never able to get any kind of powerful cards in my deck until it was far too late and we were only turns away from ending the game.

Not bad, but no desire to purchase myself. I would play again but only if there was nothing better opening up at another table.

Edit June 2015: Replayed a few times more as a focus game at EBGL. Definitely felt more enjoyable this time around, bumping to a 6.5.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Legendary is broken. It's because it's a "competitive co-op" game, rather than pure co-op. This generates a huge free rider problem. The player who spends the whole game ignoring the mastermind and just going for the personal-gain villain kills will win. Seriously, go ahead and try it this way. Just let the other players kill the mastermind while you concentrate solely on your own VP. If everyone loses, oh well. But if there's a winner, it's damn near sure to be the most selfish player who helped the least on the mastermind. That's a broken game design in my opinion.

Now, if there was a way for the other players to screw you over and/or kill you for not helping enough, that would partially address the mechanical problem, but would only break the thematic aspect even more than it already is. There ARE ways for other players to harm you, but not enough of them to make a difference.

Oh, but it can be played as a pure co-op, which should solve the problem, right? Wrong. Pure co-op play would give you no incentive to go after the villains at all, just the mastermind, which turns it into a 1-dimensional game. In fact, it actually HELPS the players when villains escape, because you K.O. a hero from HQ, which means you can thin the pool of the heroes no one wants to recruit anyway. Seriously, the game is designed so that it helps the players when villains escape. How is that thematic?

Legendary is broken, both mechanically and thematically. I don't say that often about games, but I think it applies here. I won't likely play it again.


EDIT: Oh, and setup/teardown sucks. Seriously, it takes damn near as much time to construct all of the fiddly decks here and there and to break everything back apart later than it does to actually play the game. Long setup and teardown isn't usually a showstopper for me, but it's just the cherry on the shit-sundae here.

Not bad. A cousin to Ascension, but with Heroes and Villains coming out of separate decks and on separate tracks. Feels similar to Ascension but with the distinct twists of a cooperative game. RATING: 9
While the game doesn't do anything revolutionary with the deck-building genre, it boasts a refinement of gameplay mechanics that makes it, in my opinion, the king of deck builders. Dominion is a great game but the theme is a bore. Thunderstone is awesome too, but the theme in Legendary and the way cards combo off each other blows the former out of the water. 

The different schemes alter gameplay nicely from game to game. I especially like the Skrull Invasion scheme which puts heroes into the villain deck and allows you to add them to your deck once defeated. 

I had to take a point off for the poor quality of the components, the board and cards are all made of very cheap materials.

RATING: 9
IMHO, this is far superior to DC Deckbuilding game for a comics fan in that the various schemes and the use of the city track create a narrative — whereas DC has fantastically thematic individual cards and a fierce little game engine, but lacks that story element that I really enjoy in Legendary. I'm also firmly in the camp that this game is a cooperative game with a competitive element, exactly like Defenders of the Realm and Castle Panic. Others have argued this heatedly. To each their own. I've played the game dozens if not hundreds of times and enjoyed it with 2-4 players. It is in my Top 10.

Rated for play with kids with adjustments to Mastermind strength to make the game more challenging (and longer).  A deck builder that's simple enough for kids to enjoy and just deep enough for adults to as well.

The game's difficulty is tied to the number of players.  During games with more players, the players don't have a chance to build their decks as quickly for the same amount of elapsed villain cards.  Since victory is tied directly to elapsed villain cards, you can see how the game becomes more difficult with increased numbers of players.  I've not seen a perfect solution for this, but the game is fun none-the-less.

RATING: 5.5
I really enjoy Dominion, and was excited to try a different deck building game, but was disappointed at the quality of game play in Legendary.  The game has a great theme, but not much else.  The friends I played Legendary with are big comic book and Marvel fans and really like the game, but aesthetics and the theme of a game are not important to my game experience.  So here are some of my issues with Legendary.  
Some villian groups complement certain masterminds better than others, and if you are going to truly be random in picking the heroes that go into your pool of cards be prepared for a mastermind basically countering some of the heroes that are selected.  The game is unbalanced, either too hard or too easy (depending on how many people are playing), and has a tendency to stagnate early in the game.  Most heroes have powerful cards that cost a lot of recruitment points, but many times a couple of those cards show up early in the game on your helicarrier and no one can buy them, so you just try and make do with less card options until you can clear those cards out.  Almost worth K.Oing them which is a shame because they are supposed to be the awesome cards in the deck.  

Overall This game could have been good if they had worried more about the mechanics of the game and less about the theming.  Also they Should have gotten rid of the "semi co op" style of the game.  It doesn't add anything useful , and detracts from the already loose co op mechanics of the game.

RATING: 7.8
The packaging is awful and nonsensical. Don't be blind sided and offput by it - Just break everything down to matching pictures and don't try to figure out the arrangements.
Remove the notion of cooperative villain-bashing aside.
This game is like Dominion in that you build your deck to get VP's. The game's bosses are like Providences - they're worth more and when they're gone, the game is over.
All other villains are like a duck shoot at a carnival, point grabs.
It is like Ascension in that the card pool shifts as the other players acquire and defeat cards - so it's not the best for planning out turns while you wait.
The final/epic/most expensive versions of the Heroes can be overpowered - Hawkeye nerf please?
With that said, the game is fun and creative. Some of the hero designs are downright genius. Our final game of the night told an excellent story that'll stick with me for some time. I can easily see this as one of the games people will talk about after playing.

RATING: 7.25
Fun deck-building game, mainly co-operative but can be played to find out a final victor at the end of the game.

For theme alone, I was sucked in, as the artwork on the cards just sings Marvel.  Plenty of cards to choose from, which adds a ton of replay value.

Similar to other deck-builders, draw to max hand limit, try to utilise buying power to acquire best combinations of cards to suit your playstyle, and attack visible enemies to knock them out.

Have played one game of this where one person wouldn't take any advice, and just bought randomly (which affected how well everyone else performed).  As long as you don't have anybody like that around, you should have a great time.

RATING: 8.4
I described this game as "cooperative Dominion set in the Marvel universe." That has been enough to pique the interest of several of my geeky friends.

What I really like about this game is the straight-forward rule set. There aren't a lot of little exceptions you have to worry about, so it makes it easy for even the novice gamer to catch on quickly, and over time they clue into powerful card combos. I also like that you can change up the characters and villains so each play feels different.

The only real downside I've seen so far is the 2-player game is too easy, but it sounds like certain expansions can up the difficulty level appropriately, so that's great. All in all - two big thumbs up. This was my must-buy after the big gaming weekend with my brother.

RATING: 8
SOLO PLAY:

1 Player Minimum
5 Player Maximum
I love the theme. I love the co-op. fun game. After playing several solo games with 1 hand I think it is broken and not balanced to truly play solo. Now I solo playing 2 hands like a 2 player game.

Rules Notes:
-BURROW: If the Streets are empty place the defeated enemy in the Streets, unless they started in the Streets.
-CIRCLE OF KUNG FU: X of circle means that Villain had +X fight unless you reveal a hero of X or more. Example: "5th Circle of Kung Fu" means that Villain has +5 Attack unless you reveal a Hero with 5 or more cost.
-ESCAPE: When a Villain gets pushed out of the city. 
1.) Discard a Hero in the HQ with 6 or less cost. 
2.) Each player discards one card in their hand for every Bystander attached to escaping Villain.
3.) Activate Escape effects on escaping Villains card.
-SIX CARDS: drawn each turn.
-FOCUS: May pay the cost on the left side of the arrow to get the effect on the right side of the arrow as many times as you want.
-HEROES: Starting Shield Heroes count as Heroes.
-RISE OF THE LIVING DEAD: Each player checks the top card of thier Victory Pile. If that card has Rise of the Living Dead trait...that villain renters the city. Mastermind Tactics never return this way.
-VERSATILE: May either be Fight or Recruit. Choose when played.
-WALL CRAWL: When this hero is recruited, you may place it on top of your deck instead of your discard pile.

RATING: 4
I like the way they've structured the opposition in the game - the combining of an antagonist and a nefarious plan (each of which affects deck composition and victory, and has its own special event every so often) with some other mix-in elements looks really nice for creating a variety of interesting setups with a different feel.

The hero part of the game is... functional. It serves the purpose of making the game go, but basically felt like I was playing Ascension: The Marvel Edition. Interesting choices were vanishingly rare in the early game (purely due to what I drew from my deck) and never seemed to get beyond "infrequent" even in later game. And the game takes a lot longer to set up / break down than Ascension does.

The semi-cooperative nature didn't sit well with me; I like it in other titles, but here... eh. [Addendum after 2nd play: it seems like it's required in order to maintain tension / interest when games are obviously not going to be lost.]

I might be willing to play again - it wasn't totally un-fun, at least when played in a reasonable span of time - but all in all, I think I prefer the gameplay of Sentinels of the Multiverse, both for thematic alignment and basic interest in the mechanics. I certainly wouldn't mind if Sentinels' villain design used some of the ideas that Legendary brings to the table, though! (In all fairness, their Environment decks do some of the same good things.)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.6
Love deck building, love co-op, love Marvel... The theme is spread on this game like icing...it's everywhere. This might be the first game I own that I'll own everything that goes with it.

RATING: 8
I have played many deck building games over the years, but this is my personal favorite. The art in the base game is a bit of a let down, the expansions get much better there. Being a big Marvel fan I also this this game does a great job with the flavor of each hero. I would honestly rate this even higher but I think the game plays better once you add a couple expansions (especially some of the big box ones). Once you have at least Dark City and maybe a small expansion or two I would put this at an 8.5.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Components: The artwork is nothing special. It's not the best Marvel art I've seen; it's not the worst. But the graphic design is terrible. The board is unnecessarily huge, but with mostly just a blah background. The one place where some thematic attention was given, the five villain locations, actually looks too busy once villain cards are on those spaces.

The card design leaves a lot to be desired. The power and recruiting symbols are in the same location on the card, which causes a lot of confusion. The recruitment cost, which is only used once, is enormous, whereas the other information, used over and over, is small to miniscule. I guess the idea is that I need to be able to see the cost from across the table, but after that I can read it up close in my hand. But I need to read what the card does to know if I want to buy it, and even in my hand the symbols in the top left and the special power text are way too small.

The rules are ambiguous on many points, especially with regard to playing cards from my hand.

Experience: Still waiting for that great superhero game. This isn't it. There is no tension during my turn. I play all my cards, use their full recruitment cost, their full attack power, all their special powers, buy a bunch of cards, defeat a bunch of villains, rinse and repeat.

The only two interesting decisions were which icons to specialize in, and whether it was worth the risk to go up against the Hydra (who reveals two additional villain cards). Fighting villains seemed to have mostly positive consequences, layered on top of the fact that we were already winning.

Is this really supposed to be cooperative? Seems like it couldn't make up it's mind. It's virtually identical to Thunderstone in skeletal structure, but with the added caveat that we could all lose. Doesn't seem much different from Terra and Defenders of the Realm in that regard.

The super powers are mostly lame. The game has too simple a core engine to sufficiently differentiate the heroes. Thematically, some of the mechanisms are really cool. I like how the villains can capture bystanders, and someone like Spider-Man (as opposed to Wolverine) is able to rescue them. But what does Cyclops getting rid of a card have to do with activating his power? And Wolverine drawing cards when he gets riled up doesn't really fit with the idea in the comics that he works best when he works alone.

The mastermind scheme mechanism, similar to the advancing threats in Space Alert, is great in theory (except for the fact that we can see his entire plan ahead of time, which doesn't fit with the theme), but here doesn't result in being very interesting.

The baddies are pushovers. After the first few turns, we were regularly beating two villains a turn. The punishment for a villain escaping is a non-factor. Wounds were seldom seen.

Seems a lot like a mass-marketing effort to cash in on a popular game mechanism, but relying more on the Marvel brand than on fun play.

Eagerness to Play Again: No Desire

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Legendary is one of my favorite games of all time. Deckbuilders are my favorite type of game and putting Marvel with it was a huge win to me. I love the theme and feel of the game (although I'm not a comic book nerd, so I don't necessarily know the connections with all of the heroes and villains). I could play this just about any time a group is looking for a game, and when they're not, I'll oftentimes pull it out to play solo when I can.

There are some cons, but it's up to you whether those cons are enough for you to avoid it. The base set is pretty easy once you get mechanics figured out. If you want a game you'll win most of the time and you just want the challenge of outscoring your friends, then you won't care. Part of the fun for me is the very real threat of losing so I would highly recommend Dark City as a go to expansion as it adds a lot more variety and ramps up difficulty. Also, playing with 5 players is possible, but it gets pretty long and slow at times. Also, you really start running into each other as you try to recruit your heroes. This can happen with 2-3 players, but it's easier to work with each other to stick with a specific hero or two to optimize your deck. Sometimes with 5 players, you're really just left with either wasting a turn, or taking that one hero that doesn't totally fit your deck and that someone else really wants. 5 players is also tough in that you have to draw through 10 villain cards before the group has gone through their starter decks. Depending on the shuffle and villain groups, you could potentially have 5 villains escape before anyone can even hope to touch them. We do a house rule to help offset this if we have 5 and we just skip drawing a villain on our very first turn so that we at least have a shot. To me, the sweet spot for this game is 3 players, although 2 and 4 can be equally fun. There is some randomness to the game so if you hate that, this might not be a great pick for you. To me, it's part of the challenge as I can't just go build my deck how I want while ignoring other players (ex. Dominion). Also, I like the art, but I know that some of the female characters can be a bit over the top with cleavage, huge boobs, and super tight outfits. If you're familiar with the comic versions of Storm, Emma Frost, Rogue, etc., then this won't be a shock. You can Google the artwork if you are concerned about that. I can see how some might not want their 14 YO son staring at some of the cards.

There is no perfect game and everything will have some drawbacks. To me, these don't impact me enough to keep me from playing it over and over. I've played it at least 100 times and it doesn't get old because there is SO much replayability due to changing the scheme, mastermind, villains, and heroes. I used to play this over lunch at my work. The 4 of us could play a game consistently within an hour (Plus 20 min setup and tear down).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This game is really good deck building game, perhaps not as complex as Dominion, but I think its more enjoyable, and I prefer the superhero theme to the land baron theme (just my opinion).  Those familiar with other Deck building games like the affore mentions Dominion or Ascension, you start with a small weak hand of cards and buy cards to make it better.  The mechanic works great for this style of game, and I love the cards, even though the artwork is a little repetitive, that didn't bother me at all.  However, there is only one small problem that you will have to deal with if you decide to buy this game, and they will probably fix in later expansions, but for now, its up to you.  And this is in scaling.  What is scaling?  I believe the range of players for this game is 2-5, with added solo rules as well, so lets just say 1-5.  The game is basically harder the more players you have, similar to other co-op games like Pandemic and Forbidden Island.  Like those games, the villains go every time a player goes, and in the beginning before you build a decent deck to start fighting off minions, you have to let a few go.  In a 2 or 3 player game its no big deal, in a solo game, its nothing, but in a 4 or 5 player game those guys are going to start stacking up quickly, making it harder and harder for you to win, or even get a shot at fighting the mastermind.

So, to fully enjoy this game, you can either just play it with 2-3 players, OR, you will have to take care of the scaling issue yourself.  BoardgameGeek offers several fan variants for making solo play harder, and other variants to make the first few round of 4-5 player games manageable.

The first time we played this was with 2 players, and it was a cakewalk, and I said, this game is too easy, then I played a few solo games, and it was even easier, so I change a few rules to make it harder, and then when we played with a 4 player game, we lost badly with the new rules, switched back to the original rules we won, but there were a few close tense moments.

So, take home point, this game is amazing to play, I find it much more enjoyable than Dominion or Ascension, but playing it with 1 or 2 players, you may need to add a little challenge otherwise, it will seem too easy.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
Legendary is mostly cooperative deckbuilding game with a shifting line of cards and combat/purchase resources ala Ascension. The difference is the cooperative nature and that it has two lines of cards. One for purchase and one for combating. It also has a boss ala the Cerberus Engine deckbuilding games. I don't really like the semi-coop aspect of: we are all trying to beat the boss, but if I get the most points for different things, I am the ultimate winner. Thankfully, when playing with harder bosses, it's basically a fully cooperative game. One negative I will say about the base game is that all of the artwork for each hero is the same despite cards having different effects. This is really annoying. I hear that it's been fixed in future expansions, but none of the other true expansions (I'm not counting Legendary Villains) have been stand alone. So, even if this was really awesome for me, I would be stuck using these heroes or buying a lot of content for base game components. Neither of those propositions appeal to me. It's a moot point though, because while the actual game doesn't take too long, the setup and takedown of this game is a massive undertaking. I would much rather play Ascension or a Cerberus game if I wanted a similar deckbuilding feel, Pandemic if I wanted a coop, or Aeon's End if I wanted a deckbuilding coop game where you have to beat a boss.

RATING: 5
+Variable setup and the many different strategies you can create with the same group of heroes creates great replayability
+Love the theme
+Wide variety of synergies both explicit and more subtle

-Rewards for killing villains allow the rich to get richer
-Random draw from hero deck can hinder a player from furthering their strategy partway through the game
-Lucky recruit draws early on create a snowball effect
-I liked the semi coop for a while but am realizing it's really not quite the elegant solution as it seemed. When the popular backlash against the base game was people refusing to play semi-coop and playing fully coop instead, the expansions became more and more difficult, making semi coop not a viable option. The expansions are the only way to add a little more meat to the game but then you have to give up on the semi-coop and still have these awkward cards that reward attacking your team-mates. Really just not elegant design, UpperDeck should have stuck to their guns on semi-coop or really endorsed fully cooperative play. Instead the game is awkwardly in between and I just want to get Dominion instead.
-Also it's terrible that with one big box expansion all the cards will fit in the expansion box but not the base game box, while the board will fit in the base game box but not the expansion box.

Expansions Owned: Dark City
(Sleeved in UltraPro Black Mattes)
(CheapMagicSleeves.com good price for future expansion purchases)

Location: Oberlin

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
(Rating including expansions: [thing=137762]Dark City[/thing], [thing=142020]Fantastic Four[/thing])

One of my favorite deckbuilding games right now (and I don't even care much for superheroes). I really like the variety in this one. Different superheroes, masterminds, villains, henchmen and schemes make each game unique. It's extremely streamlined, but this grants you total freedom during your turn. You have unlimited buys and attacks you can spend your resources on and you can interchangeably use them. Great, great fun! Depending on your playgroup, you can either play it semi-cooperative or fully cooperative.

It does have its negative points though: Setup and teardown take some time and require extensive shuffling to prepare the hero and villan decks. Because of this, I recommend sleeveing the cards, which is something I normally don't do, as they will show wear quickly. And I don't recommend playing with 5 players, because it's pretty tough. Chances are that by the time everyone's had their two starting turns, 3-4 villains have already escaped.

RATING: 5
Really nice idea but not great execution. 

The HQ full of the shuffled together heroes is nice as you cannot guarantee what will be available for your turn, likewise with the villain deck you don't know what is likely to happen on your turn, will the master mind attack ,or advance his scheme, will a villain or henchman turn up, or does a bystander get themselves into trouble. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Fun, thematic, playable deck-builder.  I dock it a full rating point due to it being too easy as a solo or coop game (most of my plays are solitaire, and even the advanced solo mode is easy to win 90%+ of the time).

It also feels a bit odd having multiple characters, and having certain cards 'KO'ed' from your HQ, but the character is not actually KO'ed.  Just one of his cards.  There's a lot of disconnect between the player and the heroes, especially in multi-player since everyone is playing the same heroes.  I'd prefer a more RPG-like play style, which would also allow for campaign play.

Some of the mechanics are a bit wonky.  Villians escaping the city (with or without captured civilians) is a huge deal in certain scenarios, but often it doesn't really matter at all, even though it is supposedly one of the main things the heros should try to prevent.

A decent game, but not my ultimate Marvel card game by any stretch.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Played 9 times with 1,2,3,5 players for 6+ hours.
Ratings history: 7,8,7,8,7

Play #1, JUL 2013: Honestly, this game was played with 4 experienced players who were just killing time, and they raced through teaching me the game - so I really had no idea what I was doing, or really what was going on at all. I just heard lots of complaints about how badly we were doing.

Play #2 and #3, DEC 2013: Played with 2 and 3 players and...I don't know I just don't enjoy this game all that much. With two players there are 5 hero card-sets and less cycling through, so it's harder to make a good deck. Why would I want to play a game that makes me build build worse decks the fewer players I have. Gameplay a little boring, and I feel like the decks and decisions I make have very little control - a feeling I don't get while playing Dominion. I guess I just prefer the variety and control of Dominion more than the theme and license of Legendary.

Play #4, APR 2014: Found a used copy for a price I could pass up, and played it three players - and loved it. The complaints I had above may be valid for 2 players, but today's 3er was fun. Yes the game is Dominion co-op lite, but great for what it is.

Play #5 and #6: Played my first two solitaire games and found it reasonably fun. I do agree with those people who say that the base game is VERY simple - even simpler than Dominion's core set. Solitaire is when I really notice the (relatively) simple deckbuilding of Legendary.

Plays #7-9: As a solitaire game, this game is too simple and scattered. I had a game where I'd already built a strong red/yellow deck...and then had nothing but green, black, and blue cards available to buy. To the best of my knowledge, you can only cycle heroes when you buy one, or when you KO one as a result of of a Scheme Twist...so a Scheme with few Twists results in no/low turnover. For solitaire play, I'll stick with Lord of the Rings The Card Game.

MAY 2014: It's just too simple, and the SHIELD cards occupy too much game space for too long in the game, which detracts both from fun gameplay and from theme.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Low trade priority.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
A better Ascension.  Because, the cards of Ascension are more complicated and often create enormous links of cards (with 5 players I have seen 3 of the 5 during each of their turns, playing as many as 30+ cards each time) which chokes the game and can make it quite boring.  Because the Ascension cards are more complicated, It takes longer to decide which card to purchase and longer to  play, especially when a player is less familiar with the cards.  The player who wins is often the player who knows the cards best.

Legendary has good strategy, and snappier purchase and attack.  Hard decisions occur when a player has to decide between when & how to help a fellow player, and when to help only himself.  (If the game wins, everyone loses, yet if the players win, one player wins the "mostest".

I would have rated Legendary higher, but the card design is very poor making sorting of the cards very difficult, and therefore unnecessarily extending setup/storing time.  The design problem, especially with the Villains' decks, is that the decks' title is so small & faint and often merges with the background illustration so that the mandatory sorting simply takes too long.  There should either be a more easily read deck title or better yet, a prominent symbol for fast sorting.  I want to play the game, I don't want extensive down time setting it up and putting it away.

It is such a problem, I hesitate to buy the first printing of this game, thinking, hoping, that Upper Deck will fix the problem with a second printing.  Otherwise I really like the game, want to own a revised edition, and am looking forward to expansions.

Others complained that the Hero decks could be more interesting, wishing that each card would have a different pose of that Hero.  That doesn't bother me so much because it doesn't effect play or lengthen the game--it is just a more desirable esthetic.

RATING: 6
While I enjoyed the game I played, I didn't experience anything drastically engaging during the game.  There's nothing fundamentally wrong with Legendary.  It's a beautifully presented deck building game with the familiar mechanics for this genre of game.  There's a few things which are different from other games: how the game ends, how to build your deck considering the challenges on the board, and the game can actually beat all the players so they have to cooperate competitively so to speak.  Players who are Comics fans and are looking for a game in this genre won't be disappointed; experienced players who have already played Dominion, Thunderstone, Ascension and etc, won't find anything new apart from the super cool art.

RATING: 10
One of my favorite games. 3-4 players is the sweet spot. With two, it's generally easier to defeat the Mastermind so it's more competitive between the players. With 5, it can be extremely difficult and almost has to be played as a pure co-op. Set-up and packing up are both a giant pain, which is why it's a good idea to play at least twice, so you get more enjoyment for your effort. :)

I have most of the expansions, and there has been some definite "power creep" with the new Masterminds. Not so much with the Heroes: base game characters like Thor and Cyclops still pack a huge punch. I think I'm going to pass on [thing=156689]Villains:[/thing] playing as super-villains just doesn't do much for me.

All plays recorded under the base game. I recommend using a randomizer (app or online) for your card selection. I prefer Legendary Randomiser for Android, but there are plenty of good ones out there. I'm embarking on some solo plays to try everything out and experiement with some more thematic setups (an all-Civil War game, for example).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Strongly prefer 3 players or less. Makes the game feel less solitaire, reduces the downtime between your turns, and you feel like you have a bigger impact since you will usually get a turn before a villain escapes (in a 5 player game, it's more likely the villain might escape before you even have a chance to fight it).

Pros
-Good variability between games (lots of heroes, villains, scenarios, masterminds)
-Can be played solo, coop or semi-coop
-Card abilities replicate hero abilities very well and scenarios are fairly thematic
-Gameplay feels very fluid and combo chains are rewarding
-Simple to teach, relatively short play time
-An easy play, not much thought needs to go into it, most choices are fairly obvious (can be a con depending on group/mood/preference)
-Easy to scale difficulty

Cons
-Hassle to setup and re-sort
-Depending on scenario, some core game effects and mechanics have little to no impact (e.g. villains escaping can either be a loss condition, or have no noticeable effect)
-Semi-coop gameplay breaks theme (why are superheroes competing with each other to take down a villain?)
-Not all team affiliations well supported (e.g. 1/3 game is X-Men, but there is only 1 Spider-Friends character...unless you buy their expansion of course).
-Weird design where certain Masterminds (the ones from the core set, some others) give you benefits for defeating them, but some Masterminds punish you for defeating them (the ones from Dark Cities, some others). Seems very arbitrary.
-Villains (and some hero cards) are generally not very memorable, and the effects usually just feel pasted on (a case of mechanics come before game/theme).

RATING: 6
Deck building review comparing the game to Dominion after one play.
It is an appealing design and intriging theme with alot of variation in set up. Pick a evil mastermind, a scenario and get some of many superhero decks to play with. 

It is semi-cooperative but we played it as a competitive game and the cooperative part which I usually hate in this game I dont mind. 

+ Wounds in deck that can be used by some heros is in theory a fine concept. 
+ Enemies travel on board and you may kill them easier on some spots, that is a nice concept. 
+ Enemies that get away hurt you in some way, a concept that puts some pressure on the players.
- Not that important to kill them off though, and hardly ever any interesting choises of which enemy to kill. 

- Longer game with less improvements in deck. 
- Fewer options than Dominion. 
- Fewer and less interesting synnergies 
- Some turns you cannot do anything. May be only too expansive to buy a card and too hard to kill a bad guy, 
- Bonuses on cards that only take effect if you have already played one card of that type is missleading and annoying. 
- Few options for cards to buy lead to that you only buy the one you can buy. 
- Luck of the draw plays a big part as even if you have managed to get 2 cards of the same type (which will take a long time) you have less than 50% chance to draw both on the same turn. 
- Lots of wounds dealt out if a player use a powerful and unfair Hulk card. There is almost no way to come back from that for other players. 

Conclusion: 
Fun to play a deck builder again, was a long time ago. Better theme and design than Dominion and feels newer more evolved in some ways. But very few interesting choices per time makes it a quite boring game with way too much luck and often only obious and bad choices make me rather want to play dominion even though I am tired of that game....will look for other deck builder with less luck and more choices.

RATING: 6
I am not totally convinced this deckbuilder is balanced. A few cards in the right place seem to guarantee wins. However, the coop/competitive element comes off really well, and it always feels close before the push to victory begins. Lots of theming too, and lots of room to expand with new stuff.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Most similar to Ascention in terms of game play but with 2 rows of cards to "buy" - a Villain line of cards that you fight using your combat factors, and a Heroes line of cards that you buy using your influence points. The plus, and point of difference is that the game is playing against you adding tension and more decision points - each reveal from the Villain deck has consequences as well as providing another target for you to beat up on and gain VP's. The main problem is that the game does not progress very well - initially your deck is weak but once your deck gets a few of the non-starter cards, it powers up quickly and the game has little chance of defeating you. Playing co-operatively (to defeat the game) as well as competitively (to score the most VP) at the same time can be a little odd.

The art is very good even if they have skimped a little by repeating the same picture for cards with different effects, although this does actually aid game play and set-up. Some text on cards is also a bit hard to read, particularly card names written in yellow over bright background colours was a poor graphic design choice. The board is excellent and aids play.

And of course, Super Heroes and Villans are always fun. Very good.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I wish I liked this one more. I certainly like the theme and the "conveyor belt" of villains is a nice mechanic. You definitely want to catch the villains before they escape, but then again, the penalty isn't too horrible since it gets you to clear a not-so-great hero on the tableau.

I like the artwork, but it is hard to read some of the text that overlays the busy artwork. The icons could be a little bigger as well, since they are important to track and make combos.

Nothing really sets this game apart for me and while the theme is ok, it's not enough to keep me engaged. Also, the set-up time is a little brutal.


=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
+ Secret Wars Expansion.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Update: This has continued to play well, into double-digit plays now. The schemes are a little thing that really make each time "feel" different, and require slightly new tactics each time. Not to overstate it, it's not a huge thing, but it does help the theme a lot. The various heroes also play very differently. Overall, a lot of fun space to explore.

The only complaint would be that the difficulty of beating the mastermind is too variable. In something like Pandemic, you will occasionally get a bad shuffle, and the game slaughters you. Here in Legendary, because of the combination of mastermind and scheme, plus the randomness of the villain deck, that sort of thing happens fairly frequently. It's not a bad thing to lose when it's close, but to get wiped out without a chance is no fun.

That, and obviously the tiny text and yellow font on top of busy graphics. It's a terrible design for user experience.

-----
I am in no way a comic book fan, but this is better than Ascension, which is the obvious comparison, because the theme is actually evident and pretty well done. Nice simple take on deck-building, and the villain deck system works very well and feels like the mastermind is building up to something.

One interesting part is that the villains (the point cards) don't go into your deck. So there's no downside to killing small point guys, whereas in other deckbuilders they would clog up your deck. I don't know if it's a good or bad feature, but it's interesting. The benefit of point cards going into your deck has always been that it prevents an early leader from getting too far ahead, because the point cards drag him down.

RATING: 6
Mixed feelings.

I think this game is thematic, and the artwork is great.  The cards are tough to read with tiny icons.

There really aren't a lot of decisions to make in this game; most turns (not all), the board presents an obvious choice.  Combine this with the huge setup effort, and you could have a worst case scenario of 30 minutes setup, 90 minute game, and maybe 3-5 significant choices.  Not a good payoff for time spent.  Although I've said the game is thematic, this is not an "experience" game where the theme can outweigh these drawbacks.

Rating is for a 2 player game.  Heck, maybe even solo.

I rate the 4-player game at a 2.  You wait longer between decisions, the game takes longer, and there is zero chance to plan ahead because the board state changes so much.  An hour of dull pain.

RATING: 5

My wife who has 20/20 vision asked time and again what each card did; she was sick of leaning across the board to read the 6pt card titles.

As game play I withhold judgement until further plays are in.

After playing this four times, I think it's safe to rate it now, but this review will most certainly fluctuate as I accumulate more plays. I like the game, but the setup and breakdown time is an issue, especially for a game where you can lose the scenario in the first 8-10 turns. As a solo game, it's very good, but with multiple players it bogs down a bit. I prefer a quicker experience and in this regard, Dominion beats it as a deck building multi-player experience, at least for me.

RATING: 5
The way the decks are built is an interesting blend of Dominion-style (only some cards are in the game, but you can acquire whichever of those you want) and Ascension-style (all cards are in the game, but a tiny fraction are available at any given time) deckbuilders. But the cards don't seem to DO very much. You scale up to trying to punch real hard, and you get there in time or not.

And it seems to have the Sentinels problem, where some variable setups are just better than others, so adjusting the difficulty level of the game properly requires lots of experience with the game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Mediocre deck building game. There is virtually no theme. I know lots of people claim this game has theme but they are all unilaterally wrong.

The players work together to defeat the main bad guy by defeating villains as they appear and by purchasing cards for their decks (so they can be more efficient at defeating villains and get higher priced cards for their decks ad nauseum).

This works mechanically but doesn't work thematically. Players do not take on the role of Spiderman, Daredevil or other favorite heroes of the Marvel universe. Players can purchase a Spiderman card for their deck so they can get a "buy" icon and/or a "fight" icon. This allows all players to more or less play Spiderman. And all players are allowed to buy Colossus cards, Electra cards, etc. So players aren't really playing the roles of their favorite superheroes. 

Furthermore, the villains move along a track as they appear. They all start in the sewers. Then they all move to the bank, the roofs, the streets and then the bridge. After that, they "escape". This means there is a constant villain parade from the sewers to the bridge out of town. How stupid! To add insult to stupidity, the SAME villain can be on different locations at the same time! Oh no, Doctor Octopus is on the roofs! But he's also at the bank! And he's on the bridge out of town! I can defeat him on the roofs but he still escapes because he's on the bridge out of town.

Why couldn't they make this game so that each player was one particular Marvel superhero? And you could purchase upgrade cards that would feel thematic to that particular hero? 

And why are the villains on a stupid parade from the sewers of New York to the Brooklyn Bridge?


Did I say, "mediocre deck building game"? I meant "shitty deck building game".

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
Legendary is [i]yet another[/i] deck-builder (my least favorite mechanic at the time of writing this). I say this because Legendary does little to differentiate itself positively from other deck-builders on the market: its biggest selling point is a unevenly applied coat of superhero paint (if that's your thing).

Above and beyond the usual tedium of deck-building games (which this game achieves in spades by bloating the usual structure with far more text than necessary and difficult to garner iconography), Legendary felt, like a comic book, to already have the outcome decided before the game begins: you know the heroes are going to win. At no point in this "semi-cooperative" game is a player going to tank it for the others (partially by structure, partially thematically) so there's no real leverage to apply to prevent the leader from continuing to lead.

Derivative, drab, dull.

RATING: 6

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I used to play Magic: the Gathering with Devin Low in Milford, CT at a comic shop called "Barrons".  He's a nice guy.

That being said I both love and hate this game.  

My Loves include the fact that it's dripping with theme.  The villain run away mechanic was something I had never encountered in a game up until then and I always thought it was neat. Also, I liked the KO cards for a deck building game, gave the feel that you were wounded in combat. 

Dislikes:  The fact that it's a semico-op game, but that's minor.  I was introduced to deckbuilding games via Ascension so my biggest gripe with this game is that there is no "cultist" card as well as no generic "heavy infantry" style card.  There have been many times when my opening hand would be 4 recruit power and 2 attack power and I get get the feeling that I just can't do anything.  In Ascension poor opening hands felt much less crippling than it did in this game. 

Conclusion:  At first my friends and I loved playing it because we loved the theme.  However, after many plays where people felt like they had nothing to do on their turn b/c the villains were too strong and we had no way of getting the power to defeat them we began to sour on it.  I still think the game is good but there are many games, and even a few deck builders, I'd rather play over it.

The biggest weakness of the game is it takes awhile to setup, and put away. I don't consider that a big problem.

RATING: 6
I didn't expect much going into this game, as I've always viewed comics & supers as vapid drivel soap operas for tween boys, but this game was a very pleasant surprise. It helped that the guy who owns the game is really into comics, and he explained some of the backstories with appropriate gusto.

Pretty good mechanics. Very good board design space. Excellent flavor. We'll see how it wears after repeated plays.

RATING: 7
This is an interesting take on deck-building, dripping with lots of theme from the Marvel comic-book universe, blending together "heros" and "villains" from the worlds of X-Men, Fantastic 4, and others.

Gameplay is relatively simple, starting with 8x recruiting cards/points (essentially money in the Dominion universe) and 4x hero cards which are "fight points". Fight points is sort of another currency that you must accumulate to defeat the various villains that crop up every turn. Each turn starts with a draw hand of six cards, and then the player can either/both recruit new heros (increasing their recruiting power or fight points) or/and fight villains.

The more powerful hero cards come out one at a time at random each turn. Higher cost heros obviously have more capability, either in terms of helping in recruiting or drawing of more cards from the player's draw deck, or helping in terms of fight points. They also have two icons indicating their affiliation and skill group. If on a draw there are cards indicating shared affiliation (such as two cards being part of the Fantastic 4) or shared skill group (such as two cards having the same green strength symbol), the card "powers up" resulting in more recruiting or fighting points.

Villains come out one at a time at random each turn also. They can be defeated if a player can play enough fight points as indicated on the villain's card. Defeated villains are VP, and sometimes come with "bystanders", which are usually more VP. If a player has enough fight points, they can go after a Master villain, for even more VP. However, most times, defeating a villain has consequences, such as spawning more villains, or forcing players to discard or "K.O." hero cards from their decks. The villain cards follow a linear track, marching along a number of spaces, and if not defeated end up in an "Escaped Villain" pile. Unlike Dominion, the villains/VP go into a separate pile, so the play deck is never saturated with useless cards ("Wounds", sort of like curses, being an exception).

As with Dominion, players try to K.O. as many of their base cards, in order to thin the deck. There are various mechanisms that allow a player to do that, but mostly it is involuntary as a result of defeating villains. There are generally two strategies to pursue: 1) build a powerful recruiting deck, or 2) build a powerful fighting deck. The first strategy seems to be the common sense approach, but the game has a time-clock mechanism through the escaped villain pile (if so many villains escape, the game is over with everybody losing), so players are usually forced to start building up fight points.

The game is semi-cooperative, since everyone is trying to prevent as many villains from escaping. However, there are some competitive aspects, as well as collective punitive effects when defeating a powerful villain. The game plays relatively quickly, as card play is intuitive if you're familiar with other deck-building games. The only confusing part may be the various interactions that are listed on the cards, as well as the various upkeep actions that must be performed each turn.

The production values are very good, with outstanding graphics on each card.

Setup is a pain with this design, as it is dependent on the number of players (this can handle up to 5 players, but possibly more with the expansion), and the specific card mix can be somewhat involved based on "schemes" (which is a scenario), which enables high re-playabilty. Takedown is equally a pain, as the various cards need to be sorted back into their specific piles. All in all, it was a mildly pleasant deck-building, but nothing earth-shattering experience in terms of mechanics. I cannot help but think this is a "dumbed down" version of Dominion. Because of the theme, and somewhat simplified gameplay, this seems aimed at the teenager crowd. It's a "7".

RATING: 7.5
This game is Dominion + Fun. I am not a superhero comic fan but there is something at more fun about this game than there is with Dominion. With Dominion people tend to have their heads down concentrating on their own thing, but with Legendary the players are watching and talking about the game during other people's turns.

There are two aspects of the game we repeatedly trip up on. Firstly in our hurry to get started we often get something wrong when building the villain deck (such as forgetting the Master Strikes or Scheme Twists). Secondly we generally have trouble remembering the steps to take when a villain escapes (with or without a bystander). The solution for the first problem is take your time and have someone double check what you are doing.  The second problem could have been avoided if the there was some player aid text next to the Villain Escapes box on the board.

After 10 plays I think it is more an experience game than a game of skill. There are 2 decisions each turn: who to recruit and who to kill. There tends to be more choice about recruitment but the consequences of the decisions are delayed (as is common to deck building games) and for combinations of cards there is a significant chance that they will not happen.  The choice of who to kill has a more direct relation to VP and game end but the choice is often more limited. So strategy may be more an appearance than reality.

RATING: 8.5
Solid (semi) co-op deck-builder with a super hero theme. Simpler than it may look at first, while bringing a couple of fresh ideas to the table: the mastermind is a non human AI that fights back and comes with its own deck, plot, strikes, etc; then you have multiple hero-villain confrontation locations, that affect the way certain villains behave, then the bystander capturing system, etc...all neat ideas that put a twist on the standard deck-builder system, without altering its core mechanics. Variable hero & villain deck content helps keeping a good level of replayability, even with just the base game. Overall: fun & easy to play.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
I love, love, love this game - simply can't get enough. Probably my most-played title at this point.

Look, I'm not blind. I can see the flaws, and I recognize that this is not, objectively speaking, the tightest or best-designed game out there. Setup and teardown are an annoying chore and a half; the included organizer and dividers are insufficient as soon as you add a single expansion; the art is inconsistent (and some is downright awful); the beginning of a game can leave you feeling frustratingly underpowered; and the theme sometimes breaks down with the mechanics.

But I love Marvel (comics AND film), which adds a lot of geeky enjoyment, and I think the game actually stands on its own.

First of all, you know what characters come in this base set? Iron Man, Captain America, Hulk. Spider-man. Wolverine, Cyclops, Storm, and Jean Grey. Let's take a moment and praise Upper Deck and Marvel for not packing this full of unknown nobodies and selling the A-list heroes as expansion packs: the base comes with a heaping of the characters you want. Respect.

As far as gameplay, the co-op element works well for a deckbuilder, the slow start makes some thematic sense (gotta put your team together to respond to the villain, right??), and once you chain together a monster hand, you feel like you're in the middle of a page of comic book action.

On top of which, there is MASSIVE replayability and variety right out of the base, and the expansions all slot in pretty well.

I play the heck out of this solo (though not every mastermind/scheme/hero works in solo play).

If you like deckbuilders, it's probably work a look, and if you like Marvel, this is a must buy.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

I felt like the game took pride in its theme and used that to justify the lack of quality in the mechanics and content - "resting on their laurels" or their marvels, I guess.

RATING: 7.5
Rating simply the base set, its a fun game offering a co-op deck builder.  As someone who is considered intermediate by most, and likely still leaning more towards novice when considered by board game hobbyists, i can say the game is simply to easy.

My girlfriend and I played it for the first time ever and simply put, won easily.  I then played the solo variant of the game and it was hardly a task even with a randomizer.  

I really enjoy the large pool of characters just in the base game, the playing mat/board, the ability to lose in many different ways, the co-op gameplay, the huge amount of expansions and extra content available, and some of the artwork.

My issue with the base game is the ridiculousness of how easy the game is, the price is a bit high for what you get, and some of the artwork. 

Overall i recommend the game and give it a 7.5 because though there is a ton of room to improve, theres also a ton of extra content that allows for much higher difficulty, and new avenues of gameplay.  This game receives one thumbs up.

RATING: 3
Legendary is a miserable game, both as a card game and as a deck building experience.  The art design is terrible despite the Marvel pedigree and important information isn't large enough to communicate its purpose when it's sitting in the middle of the table.  Unlike other deck builders, there's very little in the way of cheap actions you can perform each turn IE fighting a cultist in Ascension. Because it's a cooperative game, there are lose conditions but it's also a competitive game which can lead to players sabotaging the board when they're dead last.  Totally disappointing.

RATING: 9
Interesting deck builder with reasonable use of the license. Minor gripes about visual design (card title legibility mainly) belie a game with plenty of depth and yet relative ease to get into.

Random game setups provide near-infinite replayability but at a cost of very variable difficulty - easy to feel powerless and frustrated, yet also possible to find yourself crushing all before you. Notably thematic setups (X-Men vs Magneto, Avengers vs Loki) tend to be too easy.

As with many co-op games, maximum or minimum numbers of players don't quite work as hoped - generally solo is too easy and 5-player too hard.
