RATING: 8.5
Semi co-op game. Choose a villain, choose a couple of heroes and build a deck from those heroes in an attempt to defeat the villain.

If you defeat the villain the group has succeeded but you tally victory points based off saving civilians, defeating henchmen, and defeating the villain himself.

There's a bit of incentive to actually hinder other players when victory is in sight to guarantee that you get all the glory. The semi co-op nature is kind of off putting at times since it fits into the personality of some heroes but not really all so you can choose to play with that or not.

RATING: 2
I love Marvel. I love Deck Building. Should be a no brainer. I would rank this at the bottom of all the ones I've played, Thunderstone, TS advanced, Ascension, Star Trek Deck Building, Resident Evil Deck building. People say there is a theme? Cards with a picture isn't a theme. So I fight the enchantress and she lets me draw cards. That's not a theme. A theme would be if I fight her, and she takes the male hero from my hand with the lowest recruit cost and ads that to her difficulty. That would be thematic because she would have mind controlled the weakest man and makes us fight them too. There is no theme in this game. There is math with pictures of spiderman. The game doesn't have an original mechanic. The conveyer belt is thunderstone. The buy mechanic is every deck building game. And the way the cards interact is simpler then any other game. It's also not a cooperative game. If you play together you will beat the villan. After three turns its trivial to kill any guy on the board, and the villan doesn't really do anything that hurts you at all. I give this game a 2 only because it's not the WORST game I've ever played. Play Sentinels of the Multiverse. That game is far better on every level.

RATING: 3.5
2013-02-12

Initital rating: 5.5 (February 2013)

Legendary is a gorgeous and well produced  game, and I really enjoy it´s theme (although I have not read the comics), however I don’t think this will rise more on my ratings as I consider the game has more randomness that I enjoy in a strategic deck building game. The problem for me is that is has different opportunities for each player, one player can get lucky to get a hero card that is vastly more powerful than the others, and the same applies with the monsters, in my game, my opponent defeated all the early monsters and in my turn there weren’t any monster to fight (because the villain card was other than a monster) leaving me no choice but to acquire another hero card or pass. I still managed to win, but I feel that was because I was able to snatch a powerful Spider-man Card. This also happens in other deck building games, the worst of all is Resident Evil, but Thunderstone is also guilty of that. I prefer to play Dominion because it is much more fairer and strategic. Dominion is still king for me.

Another big negative is the setup and packing process, it takes a lot of time to ensure all the decks are properly shuffled.

Bottom line, Legendary is an ok game, but I won’t be buying it because I don’t want the winner of the game to be decided by a lucky draw and I feel this will happen a lot. Still the game can be fun.

Current Rating: 5.5
[hr]
2014-03-31

After another play, I’m downgrading Legendary rating. I don’t think I’m going to play this ever again as every time I have played, I have been very bored. Perhaps if it comes to iOS and only with 2 players, with more the downtime is excessive. 

Long setup time for what the game offers, VERY LONG play time, but the killer is that you can´t plan (there is no static card offering). You can only respond at the tactics level as there is luck in two levels (the Hero deck and the Villain deck that constantly changes), this is even worse with more players. Fails to grasp what made Dominion great, I miss the limitation Dominion imposes (one buy per turn, one action per turn). The semi CoOp fails as the players know who is winning. In this case the players who are losing won’t help (in most cases) against the Master Mind. In other words if I’m losing why should I help you win?  Legendary is all about fight power, that makes for very obvious decisions. 

In the category of variable card offering deck builders, Ascension is the best game I have played. Much shorter and simpler, I dig the art and it offers the same range of options than Legendary with much less luck and playtime.

Bottom line, very gorgeous and thematic game, but luck runs rampart. I won’t play it ever again. It was a huge disappointment for me.

Current Rating: 3.5

RATING: 7
Legendary offers an engaging semi-cooperative deckbuilding experience. Gameplay is fast and engaging, and things develop quickly as you build your engine. The theme is there through some smart design choices (escaped villains, bystanders, hostages, etc), and the artwork is spot on. The only significant downside to the game for me was the narrow decision space. It seems fairly obvious what to do on your turn, so the game tends to have a scripted feel. That being said, Legendary is an enjoyable game that I will generally play when given the chance.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 1
This game is incredibly disappointing. It has good art and a good license but fails to deliver. The gameplay simply isn't smooth enough and will always be remembered as a bad version of Ascension.

The game has flaws on virtually all aspects, whether it be mechanically or physically:

1) Setup: The game takes way too long to setup. This is exacerbated by the fact that you're constructing decks from small piles of cards which means that in order to properly randomize the deck you need to shuffle thoroughly, which increases the length of the setup. If you fail to do this, cards will come out in "clumps" which decreases enjoyment of the game.

2) Card design and pacing: the game pace is completely out of whack. There's no way you can build a proper deck before the end of the game, especially with larger number of players. Furthermore, it's inexplicable why cards do not have intrinsic point value like in Ascension. It removes a viable strategy and focus everything on attack power as the only way to win the game. Everybody's basically doing the same thing: building up purchase then buying attack power and hope to draw all the attack cards at the same time to be able to take down big monsters.

3) Winning condition: The "semi-coop" objective sounds good in theory but just doesn't work in reality. Because the game pacing is screwed up, it's really easy for players to fall behind in the deck building race. Those players then simply have no incentive to keep playing properly and will try to throw the game to make everyone lose. Not fun at all.

After proper reflection, I can safely say that Legendary is one of the worst deckbuilders I've ever played and can't believe such a flawed design made through playtesting. I am convinced it is a broken game and deserves a 1.

RATING: N/A
This is a semi-cooperative deck building game. Players recruit new heroes or fight the villains. Players fight a villain based only on their deck without help from other players. If they defeat the villain they can also pay to collect a bystander. The villains and bystanders give you victory points. Players can all lose if they don't defeat the boss in time. Note the cooperative interaction seems minimal and it seemed lighter than Dominion. I liked the theme and artwork and enjoyed the game.

RATING: 8
As a huge comics fan growing up, this game is a dream come true - a superhero themed board game that's actually fun to play. The theming is a bit of a stretch, as technically you're playing a faceless mastermind recruiting a team of heroes to foil the villain, as opposed to playing [i]as[/a] one of the aforementioned heroes... Despite that quirk, you still get the feeling that each hero is unique and thematically suited - Hulk is monstrously strong, but also risks damaging his teammates, Deadpool is wacky, etc. Subsequent expansions add interesting new abilities that, unfortunately, are self-contained to their respective sets. But it's still interesting to see the game continue to evolve with each new iteration.

RATING: 7
Highly flawed but fun game with lots of good ideas. It also gets bonus points due to my love of the Marvel universe. Flaws: (A) showing a card to prevent mastermind effects should instead be discard a card to prevent mastermind effects so that there is some interesting player choice, (B) there needs to be some clearing mechanisms for heroes in the HQ that nobody is taking, (C) the players have no control over some of the villain win conditions such as Unleash the Power of the Cosmic Cube, (D) deckbuilding is far too often about taking the best available card instead of strategic deckbuilding, (E) competitive co-op is meh, and (F) the difficulty of the challenges does not scale as the player decks increase in strength so the end-game is quite anti-climactic. Things I like: (1) some of the schemes change game play dramatically such as the Skrulls one or Legacy Virus and (2) a lot of the hero powers and decks feel very thematic in the way they play [although nowhere near as thematic as some of the Sentinels' heroes]

RATING: 7
Very preliminary rating of a 6. It's more likely to go up than down, but maybe not too high because I worry that this game isn't as mechanically thought through as it might have been. I do like that it's a lighter, somewhat simpler version of Thunderstone, a game I like very much but that can get bogged down in the mid- and late game with modifieritis. However, the scaling problems that BGG users have aptly identified here, coupled with the fact that, in all likelihood, most of my games of this would be 2-player rather than 3- to 4-player (where the timing and other mechanisms seem to work best) lowers the ceiling and makes the game feel like more of a missed opportunity than a success. The atrocious color/font/background choices, which are indefensible at this stage in CCG/LCG card design, impair aesthetics and legibility both and knock a full point off the rating.

Changed to 7

RATING: 9.5

My wife isn't a big Marvel fan (she tolerates the movies when I drag her to them) but she really enjoys this game, and frequently suggests playing it. Almost everyone I've introduced this game to has a great time.

RATING: 6
A semi-cooperative deck building game. First things first, I don't like semi-cooperative game. However that being said, I still enjoy Legendary. It's most likely because I'm a Marvel fanboy, but the game just takes all of the aspects that I like about Ascension and puts them into a more familiar universe. There are two main things that detract from this game for me. Firstly, I don't like about this game is that the entire game is fixated around buying power, but there is no Heavy Infantry equivalent. Secondly, there is no cultist equivalent for times when all of the monsters are being attacked. You should be able to get save some bystanders for a set amount of power, otherwise your turns are wasted. This ultimately leads to the semi-cooperative aspect going out of the window, and some players willing to devolve the game into a "tank this game" mentality as they're so far behind in scoring. With a lot of house ruling I think I would enjoy this a lot more.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Fantastic theme and art are marred by mediocre and frustrating game play.  There is potential here but it has not yet been realized.  The mastermind scaling does not work well, as in most cases the strength of the mastermind and villains remain relatively static while the heroes continually get stronger as the game progresses. The solo and 2-player cooperative games are far too easy, and a competitive 2-player game is far too luck-dependent to be satisfying, far more so even than the game that it is most clearly resembles, Ascension. As just one example, the bonus rewards for defeating a mastermind are random and widely variable, with many being nearly useless and many others being hugely beneficial. In many games, the luck of the draw on which mastermind cards you happen to defeat will determine the outcome of the game.  The game probably works best as a 4- or 5-player cooperative game, but even this would be better if the villains power scaled up over the course of the game.  On the plus side, the hero decks are generally well-designed and make thematic sense, and the scheme twist mechanism is brilliant and offers the potential for huge variability of game play without adding a single card to the game.  Moreover, the scheme twist mechanism can be easily manipulated to provide villain power scaling over the course of the game.  Unfortunately, only a few of the schemes provided in the box do this at all well.  Nevertheless, future expansions could easily address this problem, as could user-generated schemes.

RATING: 5
The idea is not bad, it's just I think it does not play well. First, the setup process is horrible because cards needs to be shuffled. Which creates another problem that you must read the cards every time they come out. At least in Rune Age and Dominion, you have to read a dozen of cards, and when you know them it's done. Another problem is that destroyed card go to the KO zone which makes storing the game even longer because you need to sort back all the cards that was used though the game

Second, the card play is very confusing. In fact, you do not play cards, you simply reveal you hand and apply all the effects, because all cards can be used for all action. For example, if a card give you points to recruit and attack, you can use it to do both. But sometimes cards get amplified by other played cards, so it becomes a bit confusing to keep track.

In the game I played, I managed not being able to attack anybody for the first 6 or 8 turn. That made the game very long and boring for me. I think starting with 12 cards (draw 6) is way too much. I liked more Rune Age for this where you start with only 8 (draw 5), so that you have chance to draw the card you bought on the next turn. Here in legendary, you must wait around 2-3 turn before getting the cards you bought.

Finally, there objective of the game are a bit boring, and there were little threat going on. It happened more than once than the master villain was actually easier to defeat than the regular villains. What kind of master villain is that.

So that game did not surprise me at all.

RATING: 8

RATING: N/A
Legendary: Marvel was the first cooperative deck building game I bought. I loved the Marvel theme and I like deck builders (see Dominion / Dale of Merchants).

However, the game is a bit on rails and there's very little interesting choice.

There really is no 'puzzle' here. It's all about building a team of heroes that allow you to do insane combos of cards and ultimately beat the mastermind.

It's a fun time passer.

I will say, don't play at any more than 3, otherwise the game drags.

For a better deckbuilder - See Xenoshyft.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Most thing about this our pretty great and thematic.

What I don't like is how you're mixing a bunch of different heroes into your deck.  This doesn't make great use of the herobuilding mechanic.  It makes some use of it because there are maybe 2-3 different types of decks you can run.  And there are a couple of combos.  But for me to really love the heck out of this game, it would have to use the deckbuilding to greater effect with how the cards interact with each other and the choices and versatility to the decks. 

Also, the luck is very strong with this one.  I like random setup but in this game the way everything is random makes the game sometimes really easy, sometimes really hard.  Certain heroes are much better against certain villains, certain villains are flat-out better than others, certain villain groups are better, certain schemes are harder, certain henchmen groups are harder.  And then there's the luck of which heroes you have paired with each other.  Then there's the luck of the draw and the the luck of which heroes are available in the trade row AND the luck of which villain cards get played when.  I've never seen such a pile of randomness in my life.

Variability - high
Replayability - medium
Strategic depth - low/medium
Thematic - medium
Art - awesome
Strategy vs luck - low
Down-time - bad
Also you have to constantly, incessantly, shuffle.

I still enjoy this game quite a bit.  Just love playing these cards.  Funny how you can still enjoy a game that has major flaws.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This game does not work well as a co-op, as not only is the game very easy, but unless a villain has an escape effect or has captured a bystander there is basically no incentive to killing them. If played competitively, killing monsters earn VPs and there seems to be more tactics in hate-buying the card your opponents wanted, but then I don't feel this game lends itself to that very well thematically. 5 players makes the card availability too chaotic and unless you negotiate allowing people to get cards they want to complete their combos your deck will become a smattering of random cards.

EDIT: All in all, Legendary's main draw is that it has schemes that change up the game significantly, but it suffers from the aforementioned discord between mechanics for semi co-op (especially since a lot of the stuff that prevent the scheme from happening don't give you a lot of VPs) and cooperative play, the lack of thematic reasoning for the icons boosting your other cards, a bloating of too many key words in the expansions while still not making each character feel wholly unique, and a horrible rich get richer due to killing stuff not bogging down your deck and a lot of fight effects benefiting you. I'm making it sound like I don't enjoy the game but I do, it just could have been so much better.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
user Logopolys had the following to say:

"I didn't like Ascension for deck building, but Legendary works despite being the same game mechanically. However, Legendary's synergies occur in multitude, as you would want from a card game like this. Hero skills and team affiliations trigger combos, and heroes (unsurprisingly) combo fantastically with themselves, making it very easy to build functional decks. Legendary also hits it out of the park for diversity: the sheer number of heroes, masterminds, villains, henchmen, and evil schemes that can be mixed together in absurd variety make for fairly fresh gameplay each time. Finally, the comic book theme shines through: the characters are incredibly clear, to the point that sometimes I'm buying heroes just because I like them, rather than if they work well in what I'm building. Good game."

This is very nearly my opinion exactly.   I've played many deckbuilders by now, of various types and pedigree.   ultimately deckbuilding works best as a part of a larger game, and pure deckbuilders are limited by being a "deckbuilder".    Still, there's a lot of fun to be had in this one, which is why it stays and around and I keep expanding it.   

Legendary "Encounters" games are technically better games.   they have more depth to their 'schemes' and more cooperation.  but the crazy combinations are why I play deckbuilders, and Marvel Legendary blows all the "encounters" games out of the water.   I have played Encounters - Firefly, Predator, Alien.   

There is a thematic disconnect to buying different cards from a hero...yup.   but that is easily overlooked with all the different combos and using powers to fight bad guys.   

Most deckbuilders have an issue where there isn't enough variety in the base set, and they really require 1 or 2 expansions to really take off.   Marvel Legendary has this, with the base set having a decent set of characters, limited villains and relying too much on the semi-coop aspect.   Later expansions make the villains much harder and bring in some fun abilities.    This is disappointing, as I have a hard time recommending base legendary to anyone, as I think it needs at least Dark City to be a decent game.     

Also the art in the base game is limited, with the same image on each of a hero's card.   at this point I don't think there will ever be a 2nd edition with new art, but it sticks out when you use the base heroes.   

Saying that, Legendary has done a good job of avoiding power creep, with base heroes still plenty powerful enough to be used right along side new heroes.

RATING: 8
[microbadge=13167][microbadge=5792]

I didn't like Ascension for deck building, but Legendary works despite being the same game mechanically.  However, Legendary's synergies occur in multitude, as you would want from a card game like this.  Hero skills and team affiliations trigger combos, and heroes (unsurprisingly) combo fantastically with themselves, making it very easy to build functional decks.  Legendary also hits it out of the park for diversity: the sheer number of heroes, masterminds, villains, henchmen, and evil schemes that can be mixed together in absurd variety make for fairly fresh gameplay each time.  Finally, the comic book theme shines through: the characters are incredibly clear, to the point that sometimes I'm buying heroes just because I like them, rather than if they work well in what I'm building.  Good game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Played many times with many set-ups and expansions.  Ok, this game is really fun for what it is... but keep in mind what it is!  It's an american-style, very swingy, lucky, super hero-themed game.  You can't go into it wanting a balanced, elegant strategy game.  The winner will rarely be determined by a long-term strategy and sound decisions.  There is a lot of randomness and the timing on the card draws will very likely determine a winner - and can do so very early in the game.  So just go into it with the idea that you're having fun "playing with a toy"... not "playing a game".  Having said that, if you can "roll with the punches" and laugh at your horrible misfortune, and not get too cocky with your undeserved wins it's a lot of fun.  Tons of fun Marvel characters to play with too!

RATING: 8
Got it, loved it, fell out of love, then back in love again. My first "deckbuilder", and being a Marvel Comics fan it was a no-brainer.

RATING: 5
I didn't think this would be for me, and it wasn't. I played a version with all expansions mixed in.

I liked the artwork on the no-core cards (core art is fine, but repeats across different cards are annoying) and the clever card names. The mechanics are interesting in places -- I dig the villain progression, and the overall variety of possible combinations in a given game is staggering -- but just dull or decent elsewhere. There's nothing here that makes me want to play Legendary over Ascension.

In two games, I had a lot of dead turns, gameplay was often so tactical that there was no point in picking up my hand until my turn rolled around, and I didn't get to contribute much to the group's success. The first game was "nothing, nothing, nothing, hey someone got a great turn and beat the mastermind." The second was nothing, engine starting, mastermind wipes hand, nothing, good hand, mastermind wipes it, repeat as needed." Sure, we won, but the ride wasn't interesting.

I like the idea of a co-op deckbuilder, and a Marvel one to boot, but I don't much like this one. I wish Legendary was for me, and I get why others like it. I didn't have a bad time playing, but that was mostly down to playing it with friends and the fun artwork. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
After about 15 plays split between 4 and 5 player, I rate this a 9.  It is a light game like dominion, but has plenty of real decisions to keep it interesting.  The art, theme, and mechanics all work well together to create a game that we keep wanting to play.  I suspect that Dominion will see greatly reduced play for quite a few months, maybe onwards.  Already looking forward to an expansion or two.  More masterminds, villains, henchmen, and especially schemes would be nice.

And so, in the first three days we got in 29 plays with 2, 3, 4, and 5 players.  The game is a keeper for us.

Game scales in number of players and difficulty with ease.  Easy to follow rules too.

Difficulty discussion is odd - does anybody read the rulebook?  There is a page on altering the difficulty.  Try Loki at 15 with 11 twists and the legacy virus, with a random set of heroes.  If you get lucky you might win. Too easy? Um, no.

After many months, I have over 300 plays of this game.  One of the best games of 2012 (with A:NetRunner and Clash of Cultures)

Now in 2016, it has not had the staying power of Netrunner or Clash. So, I moved the rating down to an 8. In our experience works great with 2, passable with 3, and not with 4 or 5

RATING: 7.03
Legendary Encounters beats this is a rather one sided fashion. I don't mind hard games. I understand co-ops are by nature hard as well. 

My issue is the lack of control I feel in playing the game. I even played it with a friend being the mastermind. I had 9 turns where I used four of them to heal, another four to only buy sidekicks if that, and one to actually have what I would consider a normal turn. My friend who played the mastermind said he felt like he really didn't have to really do anything, and we lost easily. There's difficult and there is you simply aren't winning and there is nothing on your part you can do. Ugh.

Yes, Encounters is built on the same system and can have its own swings, but Encounters engages me in a way where this one doesn't.

How much investment does the game offer? 1. The mish mashing of characters in this really does take away from the theme for me.

How consistent is it in its plays? 1 This might be kind.

How well does it handle its various player counts? 2. Seems fairly solid so far although I haven't looked at numbers. I think you need the first expansion to make it difficult anyway across multiple player counts. 

Fun? 1. A couple of games have really felt like I was doing little outside of being beaten down with no real ability on my part to change that. 

Quality game mechanics? 1.5. Will get converted to a 2, but I can't give it an honest two since again, Encounters beats this.

Overall a 7 for design. 0 for my need to own it. I'll put need to play at 3, so 7.03 overall.

RATING: 6
Deck builders typically exist in a strange, ethereal game universe where theme is legally required to be [i]nearly [/i]as thick as the air swirling about your head and most of your time is spent shuffling things.

If Legendary were about toilet inspectors or Renaissance merchants or mixing paint, it would be dull, dull, dull like Dominion or merely meh like Thunderstone and Shadowrift. Instead, it's a mildly interesting blender of competitive and cooperative with pretty pictures of superheroes.

It's not ingenious. None of the deck builders is, though some make that claim. But it is decent enough given the constraints of the genre.

The fact that you're mixing and matching various superhero powers--anybody can put Hulk or Storm or Wolverine or Spider-Man card in his deck--doesn't make a lot of sense. And the powers seem fairly random, with limited connection to the superhero, with the exception of the Hulk.

It does have Spider-Man, though his power seems to be somewhat limited. I expect that was a necessary balancing mechanism to keep his awesomeness from overpowering the other heroes and making them seem irrelevant. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
[microbadge=1714]

03-Nov-2016:  Just want to make a brief addition to mention that I only play solo using the [thread=1200976]Golden Solo Ruleset[/thread] now.  You use the 2-player setup with a couple of simple tweaks, so you get to use five heroes instead of three.  It just [i]feels[/i] like a more natural way to play alone, and it's more fun using more heroes, IMO.  There are a few odd rules combos that arise on occasion, but nothing that can't be house-ruled on the fly as to what makes sense.  Definitely recommended.

02-Jul-2015:  Legendary: Marvel is another contender in the ever-popular deckbuilding genre of boardgames.  Obviously, this is themed within the Marvel universe.  You play a group of superheroes fighting off a mastermind and his minions.

It takes some cues from the Ascension engine with two forms of "currency" and the ever changing market of hero cards to purchase.  However, it adds quite a bit of fun to the mix with a conveyor belt of enemy cards wreaking havoc on the city.  A Mastermind is in charge and must be defeated before the endgame is triggered.

Especially with Dark City expansion (but even with one or two of the smaller ones), variety is one of the main draws of this game.  There is seemingly an endless combination of heroes, masterminds, villains, and schemes.  Using just the base game, the difficulty is fairly low, but the advanced rules and plethora of options listed in the Dark City box make this game a challenge as well as full of fun.

I don't feel like any specific superhero while playing, but I think the overall theme of being a group of superheroes fighting a group of baddies definitely shines through.

Overall, the game is a blast to play, and that's why I really love this game.  I know there are other games in this series, but since I began with the Marvel version, that's probably the one I'll stick with.  If another theme tickles your fancy, then I say go for it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Galactus robbed a bank...
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
I really love the theme and the variety of cards available allow for some challenging scenarios. It really shines with the expansions which bring new ideas into the game and exponential variety. Everyone needs to defeat the villains but then can score individually at the end making it semi-cooperative.

You start off with a hand of 12 S.H.I.E.L.D. Agents, 4 with attack of 1 and 8 with recruit of 1. On your turn you basically do three things: 1 pull a villain card and follow it's text, then you play your own cards and can attack and/or recruit heroes. Of course the heroes you recruit power up your deck and provide the combos you need to defeat the villains and eventually the Mastermind.

I suppose some gamers won't love it. The cards you draw and order you play them make a difference but those decisions aren't particularly difficult. For me though it's a really fun exercise which I've enjoyed experiencing with my young son.

RATING: 4
Definitely not for me. The game is very cleverly designed to allow a variety of scenarios that customize each game in a way I've not seen in any deckbuilder before. The scenarios really push the theme into a narrative success.

However, the gameplay is rather dull. The decisions are all tactical and quite obvious, perhaps even more obvious than Thunderstone, which is saying a lot, since a player can attack and buy on the same turn. That coupled with the fact that cards can be used for their textual action as well as attack/buying power means players never have to decide between cards or uses.

Setup and teardown are as bad as its reputation claims. The semi-cooperative mechanic is always a loser in my book. Just not a good game.

RATING: 8
SOLO CAPABLE

45 Min. (longish setup)


The artwork is delightful. It would be neat if each hero had different art for their different abilities, but it's by no means a deal breaker. What I really have a problem with, is that the villain cards have text used for sorting the cards that is too small and obscured by the artwork, which makes putting the game away take probably twice as long as it should. Although it's not a deal-breaker, it's such a lame design choice it's bewildering. It will make you angry. That said, the game is fun.

Because the scenarios can swing greatly in difficulty depending on the villains and heroes used, I feel it necessary to document my plays, detailing the setups to try different tactics on sessions I lose or to tweak scenarios I find too easy. It's extra work to have to log the setup stats, but this is also the kind of game where session notes are kind of fun, and actually prove that, unlike some of the game's detractors, the theme of the game does shine through. 

An example of a note from my first solo victory:

"Good won the final showdown with 45 points. Spiderman's ability to save bystanders and Black Widow's ability to use those bystanders to add to her attack strength was a powerful combo. The Midtown Bank Robbery scheme also added many extra bystanders (bank customers) which I was able to save, thereby slowing down new villains from entering the city."

Regarding solo play:
I've played once with the official "advanced" solo variant and once with Skyzero's solo variant version 3.0. The official variant was easier to play and less fiddly, but I kept feeling like I had limited buy options, which was rarely the case in the SkyZero's variant where you play with four hero decks and put a new hero card into the HQ at the beginning of every round.

RATING: 9
There are many aspects to this game, some I very much like, others not so much. First of, I'd like to say that despite anything cons I may list, I still really enjoy this game and have given it 9 stars!

The Cons
- So, as many have found out, this game can be exceptionally easy, depending on what Mastermind, Villain groups and Heroes you choose. Depending on how you play your cards and which Heroes you decide to recruit, the Mastermind can be defeated (practically) within the first few turns, which, needless to say, can be frustrating.

- There aren't many ways (if any) in which you can stop other players from winning, other than defeating more Villains than them. Although you work together to defeat the Mastermind, in the end you count up your points to see who the final winner is, but you cannot stop the players from defeating Villains or Mastermind and there are also no methods in which the Villains that the other players may want to defeat become harder. So, if another player wishes to (and can) defeat the Mastermind or a Villain, there is nothing you can do but sit and watch them defeat said Villain.

- I have 2 separate expansions for this game and I have found they add a lot to the game. The reason this is a con is because the game is made SOO much better by the expansions and the base game does not have any of these aspects which make the game what it is without them.

The Pros
+ I have to say, the biggest pro for me is the variety! With the amount of Masterminds, Villain groups, Schemes and Heroes, you will almost never play the same game twice (unless you want to, of course) and this definitely helped me like this game even more, as you can never get bored because every game it changes! 

+ Another pro for me is the artwork! It is made in a comic book style and given these are comic book characters it really made the game seem much more...real? I'm not sure the correct word but it definitely helped the game look better!

+ This pro is the one which made the most difference with the amount of stars I have given it and that is that I really enjoy, if not love, deck-builders, so that really made the game much better for me, personally.

+ Another pro which made a huge difference is that I really enjoy Marvel! I love the thought of superheroes and defeating the bad guys!! So that is what kinda made me want to play it in the first place, the it has to be a big plus in the amount that I enjoyed the game. 

Overall, this game, for me, was a 9/10 Stars!!!!!!!!! I will continue to play this game many times in the future, probably because a) I like thinking that I am totally a superhero and b) the variety means I will never play the same game again! (or I might if I fail it and then really want to complete it and continue playing until I win!)

RATING: 9
OK. So where have I been the past few years that I am just now playing this game? 
This is a ton of fun to play.
I enjoy the cooperative deck building this game offers. 
It is a little complex at first to get going and there are plenty of rules to learn. At first, we were beating the game without any problem until we watched youtube vids and realized we had been doing some stuff wrong. 
We did have a few questions on some cards and had to go online to get some clarification. But once we got those we were off and running and having a blast.

It does take some time (10 minutes maybe) to set up but totally worth it.
Great artwork.
The board itself is large so you do need some space to play.
I also suggest getting protective sleeves for the cards because you shuffle them a lot and they could wear down.
I like that there are expansions to add too.
If you like the Marvel Universe then you will want this game. If you like cooperative gameplay you will like this game. If you like deck building you will like the game. If you like games you will like this game.

RATING: 9
One of my favorite deck builders to date. The difficulty is very inconsistent, and continues to be more so with each added expansion, but the game is always fun. If you have any interest in superheroes at all, this is one worth checking out.

UPDATE: Increasing rating to a 9. This game has only gotten better with more expansions. Initially I probably would have given this a 7 or an 8, but the content available for Legendary has really helped elevate it for me. I think I'm one of the few people out there who miss the more mild enemies from the base game though. Playing against harder masterminds is fun from time to time, but I like this game best with a more casual and semi-cooperative feel.

RATING: 5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is a very fun deck-building game with a great license.

Finally, I get a superhero board game that I can play with others and it's enjoyed by all.

Much more simpler and faster than Thunderstone, this game will most likely fully replace Thunderstone even though it's brand new and the expansions haven't rolled out yet.

I have played it with 2, 3 and 4 players and a sundry of scenarios and it has been fun even when we've all lost (damn you reckless Hulk).  

My girlfriend likes it very much, even though she hated Thunderstone.  That says something!

I don't mind the repetitive art, though obviously it would have been cooler otherwise (but more expensive) and I don't mind some of the abstract gameplay stuff, because it makes the game play smoother and still gives you the thematic flavor.

You do feel like you are a team of superheroes trying to foil the masterminds' plans.

I like to play with all Masterminds, fighting them in order of their fight value.  So the first one is Red Skull, then after beaten we switch to Magneto, then Dr. Doom then Loki.  More variety, more fun!

Go ahead and buy it and salivate at the expansions' possibilities!

Update:  
This game continues to be fun, and because it is very quick and satisfying, it has fully replaced Thunderstone and threatens any newcomers to the deckbuilding world.  Not Fantastiqa or Puzzle Strike though, because they work the mechanics in a different way.\

Update 2:
Got burned out after making variant characters and villains and all that.  To enjoy it nowadays, I have to disregard the comics part of it, because it is definitely not a simulation of Marvel comics. Basically, I have to contain myself from wanting to put every existing comic character into the game, because that would be far too time-consuming and it would never feel "right".

So, I'm still waiting for the perfect (or close to it) comics-based game, that's not a spreadsheet-needed Sentinels of the Universe.

For a casual deckbuilding game, Legendary is pretty damn fun though.

Update 3: The release of Villains renewed my interest and desire to play it.

Update 4:  With the collection of Dice Masters and the Steam port of Sentinels, and the burn-out from making custom cards and knowing that some of them are more fun than the official ones yet they do not look like the official ones (because I won't spend that much money printing them the deluxe way), I frankly don't know where I stand with Legendary.  I equally feel attracted and repulsed by it in a month-to-month basis, reason for which I haven't bought the new expansions.  I'm also not keen on co-operative games or even semi-coop, because I want a clear winner in games and not one that simply won because of the game system's manipulations.  I don't know, and it hurts.  Hope you all enjoy it better than me.

Update 5:  I'm back to liking it a lot.  I think it's an annual thing where I rediscover what I enjoy of it, then think about it and play it too much that it burns me out, until enough time passes that it feels fresh again.  It's complicated.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
Rating might be a bit harsh. This is a fine deck-building game, and lots of fun if you have affinity for the Marvel universe and are willing to invest in some expansions. The wide variety of plot cards is probably the strongest part of the game, as it creates a lot of variety in specific goals you are trying to accomplish (or avoid).

I have two problems with the game: 
(1) The "semi co-op" rules as written are pretty bad - better to play as a full co-op instead.
(2) I have a disconnect between the strong superhero theme and lack of any identity when playing the game. Why are we all collecting the same cards that showcase different superhero actions/moves? Who or what am I representing in the game? This doesn't matter from a mechanical standpoint, it's only the theme that suffers.

I'd be happy to play Legendary: Marvel if someone else is keen to suggest it, but probably wouldn't suggest it myself.

For a thematic deck builder, I prefer Thunderstone. That game system has it's own set of problems, including the generic theme, but feels more engrossing to me because I have a better sense of who I am.

RATING: 9
The Marvel Legendary system is my most played game. As about anyone will tell you, the base set needs help because it's not overly challenging. RATING: 7.8
The Legendary system is very similar to Ascension and Star Realms - that is, a light deck builder where you start with a basic deck and gradually add better and more powerful cards as you play the game.

Legendary adds a narrative/story as you play and players compete against the game itself in order to win before the failure conditions happen.  The basic idea from game to game is the same: build a deck with cards that will combo well together and produce enough attack power in a single turn in order to defeat the Mastermind.  There are a lot of different scenarios that alter the basic formula.

The game plays great solitaire, or in small groups (down time and chaos prevent me from enjoying it with greater numbers).   You can play straight co-op, solitaire or competitive.  Solitaire works really well, because you have more control over what cards to purchase and it isn't a boring 'beat your last score', but there is an actual scenario you are trying to defeat.  If you have an expansion, you can play semi-co-op with one player as a mastermind trying to beat the others.

The basic game is fairly light and without the expansions I would not enjoy it all that much.  The interactions between the cards is just too basic.  I've said the same about Dominion though, so I don't see this as a huge negative - it seems pretty typical in the hobby to have a boring but accessible base game.  Thus, I have invested in a lot of the expansion content in order to add depth, difficulty and variety.

I would play more, but the set-up is a pain.  Lots of different decks to pull together and shuffle.  So, to save time, I've just made a few different games/scenarios ahead of time and they are ready to go for play.  This gets it to the table way more often.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6.5
規則:
*每個人拿8張特務跟4張軍隊卡組成起始牌庫，並抽六張
*神盾官員，傷害，路人卡放在對應位置，隨機選一個魔頭卡，拿對應的魔頭站數卡四張蓋著放在旁邊，不同魔頭卡友一定要帶的手下
*壞人牌庫組成:隨機選一張陰謀卡，根據該卡放對應張數的陰謀扭曲卡進牌庫，加五張主要衝級卡進牌庫，根據人數選壞人團體跟羅囉團體卡，路人卡進牌庫
2p:2-1-2,3p:3-1-8,4p:3-2-8,5p:4-2-12
*英雄牌庫隨機選五個英雄組成，五人時選6個英雄，並開五張在版圖上
*每個人輪流
1.開一張壞人牌庫並結算
*如果是壞人卡就把城市的左推擺在最右邊位置，被推出去的會逃跑並棄掉英雄牌堆一張六元以下的牌(主動玩家選)，如果有人質，每個人要棄一張牌，Ambush效果一進場發動
*路人就跑到最近的壞人身上被脅持，沒壞人就跑到魔頭身上
*陰謀扭曲卡 就執行該卡並棄到KO區
*主要打擊卡 則根據魔頭卡執行，並棄到KO區
2.出所有卡，打怪(分數堆)買牌(棄牌堆)
*卡上有+記號的數字代表根據牌上條件往上加，必須在該牌之前出的才會結算
*買完牌馬上補牌，可一次多張
*打壞人時如果有fight就回先結算
*打魔頭卡則是攻擊力超過後隨機抽一張結算
*KO的英雄卡移除遊戲，可KO手上或場上的，能力可先用在KO
*拯救路人卡則直接從供應區拿
*可選擇不買牌跟打壞人來移除所有的傷害卡
*展示卡牌動作可從手中展示，或是已經出的有即可
3.抽六張，沒牌抽棄牌堆洗牌
*遊戲在四張魔頭卡打完會進行最後表演，由打完魔頭卡的下家輪流出完所有牌，總和數值最高的拿走出魔頭卡記分
*如果英雄牌庫或壞人牌庫用完還沒輸，則視為平手，分高獲勝
****調整難度可藉由增加陰謀扭曲卡數目或是調整魔頭力量來調整，新手可先替換掉部分神盾探員變成官員
***solo***
*使用三個英雄卡組成牌庫，忽略魔頭卡一定代理的壞人軍，不使用英雄大戰跟逃獄陰謀卡，壞人牌庫由一個壞人團體跟同團羅囉卡3張，1路人1個主要打擊卡，跟對應的陰謀扭曲卡，當執行陰謀扭曲卡時移除一張6以下的英雄卡
*勝利的話每個逃跑的壞人-1分，挾持走的路人-4分，每張陰謀扭曲卡-3分
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
I was obsessed with this game a year ago, always playing it as a quick filler from Euro to Euro. I still play this fun deck-builder from time to time, just not with the same intensity. What works really well in this game are the hero's powers and how they are integrated into their specific deck (Deadpool's powers are wild and have no logic to them, Daredevil's powers rely on player's intuition on "blind" draws from their deck, etc.). The game is semi-cooperative and very hard in some scenarios but it's always fun swapping out different Masterminds, Villains' Schemes, and Heroes. A bit difficult to set up quickly, but worth the time.

RATING: 7
An Ascension clone, which is not a bad thing as Ascension is fun, but this adds a bunch of bits which are arguably non-improvements. Much longer and fiddlier to setup and pack away (which is one of Ascension's strengths). It splits out the middle row into an acquisition row to enhance your deck (heroes) and a fight row to earn victory points (monsters). After that it's pretty much identical. Draw your cards, acquire as many heroes as you can, kill as many monsters as you can. Get powers that feed off each other. The whole semi co-op thing never works but at least you can from the outset choose whether to play for your team score or straight up competitively for most VPs. Its one advantage is that, similar to Sentinels of the Multiverse, you choose which villain set and which hero set to play with (hence the long setup) which at least provides some inter-game variety that Ascension lacks and allows fans of the theme to flesh the game out in their minds and ham it up a bit. Other than that, it adds little to the deckbuilding genre that we haven't already seen.

RATING: 8
Probably the best deck-builder of it's type that I've ever played. Also is a co-op. It a Super-Hero themed Thunderstone where the gametime is quicker, players deck-build Ascension-style, the villain deck reveals a card once per turn, and victory point cards don't go back into players' decks. Combos happen more than any other deck-builder of this caliber that I've ever played. Good feel to this one. Tons of replayability. Can play Solo.

Don't worry Thunderstone: you're still my favorite! But Legendary is very cool! But I must Jones Theory it out of the house. I hope someone makes a cool App of this.

Some negatives:
- Included Box Dividers for cards have no headings.
- No randomizers come with the game.
- Some of the graphic fonts are difficult to read.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
"Having played more than 40 times (many solo), I accept the argument that it doesn't work perfectly as a pure co-op...BUT I have really enjoyed it, as a pure co-op, as a 'mostly-co-op', and especially solo. The setup can make it simple or almost impossible to win. The VR solo variant is much better than the official solo rules."

What I like:
- Seems to be playable pure co-op (just adjust the difficulty)
- Fewer things to track than Sentinels of the Multiverse
- Each hero is quite different, and mostly thematic
- Solo seems to work well, especially with the "Variant Review's" variant

What I don't like:
- As with other deck management co-ops: not much player interaction
- As with other deck management games: some random setups may be problematic
- Somewhat lengthy setup and tear-down (5-10 minutes each)
- I'm not generally a fan of semi-cooperative games (co-op but with one "winner")

The comic superhero theme is neither a plus nor minus for me. Comic fans seem to really enjoy the theme.

The villains ramp up quickly, whereas the heroes takes some time to build strength. At least with 4+ players, that leads to a very unusual game flow for co-ops, where the early game is stressful, and then things (hopefully) calm down later. 

Play is pretty straightforward, although there are a lot of cards and effects. I would put the weight more like 2.5 rather than the BGG-voted 2.3.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A deck construction game built around the Marvel universe.  You draft hero cards that help you recruit or fight as you try to defeat the Mastermind before whatever Scheme they've hatched runs to fruition.  If the game suffers from anything, it's that the theme can be a stretch for some.  It's almost as if each individual player represents the same possible team of heroes in alternate universes because it's not like one player is the X-Men while another is the Avengers and still another is the Marvel Knights.

But that shouldn't get in the way of a good game for the overwhelming majority of people.  Constructing your deck to provide the right synergies between different heroes and teams can be very interesting, leading to some truly "super" turns when you've done the right recruiting and the stars of the randomizing gods line up correctly.

Fun game that can be a bit fiddly to set up if you don't get things organized well.  Used the dividers provided to sort things by name & type, then use a random number generator and a reference sheet to determine heroes, villains, mastermind, etc.  Once the game is organized, things can go pretty quickly, though you'll likely want to get 2-3 plays in every time you break it out for the setup & breakdown time.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
This game reminded me a lot of Ascension. It's also a deckbuilding game with 2 'currencies', one for fighting, one for recruiting. However in Ascension those currencies are sort of equel, as cards you recruit or also worth some points. In Legendary you wanna concentrate on good fighting cards as defeating villains or the mastermind is the only way to score points.

I think that the replayability of Legendary is greater then that of Ascension, as your deck of heroes, villains and the mastermind is different every time. But the consequence is that set-up and clean-up of Legendary will take longer as you have to create each deck at the start of your game and sort out all the cards at the end of the game.

Good thing is that there are really a lot of cards in the core set, so that you can create a lot of different sets. 

Just as with Ascension turns are quick, so playing time is short enough. The extra 'semi-co-operative aspect (like in CO2) is a nice additional feature.

RATING: 6
Better than Dominion. There are actually some strategies to develop and the choices aren't always obvious. Very easy to learn (mechanics are straightforward). After the second play I thought the game was simply too easy. What makes this game work is that the players must work together to make certain the 'bad guys' don't win but when the game is over each player scores the victory points earned during the game so there is a single winner. Some of the cards will alter the victory points earned which can alter a player's decisions during the game. 

This is not a deep game but it is fun and certainly better than Dominion.

Note: as I do not follow comic books, I played the game by the numbers and the powers on the cards. I was not even certain who some of the characters were on the cards.

RATING: 5.5
This game is not bad.  But it's not good either.  I guess if you are into the Marvel franchise it may be more interesting that it was for me.  Here's the most evident characteristics of it:
    The mechanic of the game is trivial, and it mostly a game of luck, with little tactical depth (let alone strategical).  The most annoying part being that on must either play the whole of the hand or discard it.
    The graphics are - very surprisingly for a Marvel product - below par, to the point that is easy to make mistakes while sorting the cards (that belong to some 30 different groups).
    Best characteristic: very high replayability, given the high number of combinations one can have.
    Probably an excellent game for a teenager who is not into board games, avoid if you are into the hobby and are not a Marvel fan.

RATING: 7
This is a deckbuilding game where there are several ways all players can lose against the scenario. You hire heroes to battle the badguys who run along this conveyer-belt of cards trying to escape. Players earn points for beating them, and end the game when the big boss is out of his life cards.

A big part of why I like this game is the theme. I like Marvel comics, although I have to say the costume choices they used for this are far from my favorite era.

:star: Comfortable complexity

RATING: 6
An ok game, but not great. It depends heavily on its theme, but the theme falls apart for me because it's unclear what I, the player, am in the game. I'm not a hero because I'm buying lots of different hero cards. I'm not a SHIELD agent because I'm buying other agents. It feels odd and prevents immersion in the theme.
More importantly, it feels like most of whether you will win or lose is decided in the setup and shuffling. You make lots of choices in the game, but none of them feel very meaningful. Every time I've lost the game, I can't answer the question "What could I have done differently in order to win?". The answer seems to be "Nothing, that's just how it came out". It feels a bit like the card game War in that respect.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Kind of a Dominionish deck building with coop elements. Each person cycles through a deck which has 2 main purposes - purchase a hero character from a common pool or fight an evil character that also cycles through 5 locations. Beating the evil characters give you victory points - if the henchmen can cycle off the board there is a negative impact on players.
The hero cards can work in combinations to strengthen effects or give you more draws.
The villain cards also have effects - some positive but mostly negative on your hand. There are a few cards that allows you to mess with the other players. The net is while you are building your hand the negative effects force you to dump cards so the deck building is not just a incremental progression.

The cards emphasizes form of function. There is a lot of dramatic art. However there are couple of tiny little symbols in the corners that are used for special effects. The net effect is the cards are cluttered.

An interesting game, there are several different combinations of events, henchmen and heroes (again ala Dominion) to provide variety. Better than Dominion? - in some respects yes. I like the coop element and the game timer that can cause all to lose. Also like the fact that cards can get pulled from your hand.

RATING: 9
The king of deck-builders, still my absolute favorite. The endless addons and expansions are about as annoying as they are delightful, but you only need the main game to have a great time. The competitive-cooperative balance works extremely well, as you have to be careful how greedy you are - that card you want might be really strong, but it might work better in someone else's deck, and we've had games where everyone was playing too selfishly, and the villains won.

RATING: 9
This game is great. It moves quickly and takes about forty-five minutes to an hour. Legendary offers plenty of replaybility and there are substantial expansions if you need more. There are a few problems with this game. Setup usually takes 25 minutes which is almost as long as the game itself. Tear down takes 15-20. The game seems too easy at times. Some games are won really easy without the feeling that you are anywhere near close to losing. Someone will have to try different difficulty settings to find their perfect level. This is also a reason why I like this game. It doesn't murder you every time you play like most co-ops and you feel like you can win it. Finally, many of the villains are unknowns to me which weakens the theme. I have only watched cartoons like Spiderman and Xmen growing up. I have read very few comics growing up. This causes me to look at many of the villains and henchmen and wonder who these folks are. That does detract from the immersion that I would like as I play. But all of this can still not take away from how great this game is. Great quality components and hundreds of cards for a reasonable price. 

UPDATE: So everything I have said originally is true about the base game without the cards sleeved. But I have since purchased three big box expansions and two small box expansions. I have also sleeved all my cards and printed out customized dividers. I have shortened setup and tear down substantially, and utilize Thomas Nute's randomizer app for ease of setup and the ability to get different combinations. This game is really hard now most of the time, but beatable. With the expansions this game moves up from a 7.5 to a 9, and has become one of my most played games. I don't even like co-ops, but this one is phenomenal with the expansions. *** Wife:9

RATING: 10
A cooperative deck builder with the heroes (and/or anti-heroes) of the Marvel universe taking on one of many masterminds attempting to complete a nefarious scheme. Gameplay is simple enough and does not take too long to teach. There is an amazing amount of replayability with different heroes on the team, different masterminds, different villains, and different schemes all possible to change the experience.

But it is the great deal of expansions that make this game so great. Adds various new mechanics and an outstanding host of characters to choose from. But with more expansions, it can get harder to teach since some of the mechanics need a bit of explaining. More options will also lead to taking longer to set up and put away. The board is a bit too large and I do not think it needed to get that way. The art is great on all the cards and I have found myself looking up some of the artists to see their other work. My favorite deck builder and one of my favorite games.

RATING: 8
I am a sucker for deck builders, I admit.  While not particularly innovative, Legendary is a fun light game that can be enjoyed to some degree by anyone who likes Marvel comics.  

I bought this game with my sons, now aged 11 and 14, in mind.  The art is nice to look at, and the theme attracted the boys immediately.  The rules are pretty simple - reveal an enemy, play your cards, defeat enemies and improve your deck buy recruiting new cards.  There are, obviously, more rules wrinkles than that, but it's the general idea.

The theme in the game works well.  Many of the heroes have there own "feel" (they often somewhat specialize in a certain mechanic).  Whoever designed this did a great job, in my opinion, in that the mechanic often really fits the hero.

There is quite a bit of variability in setup with each game randomly determining a Mastermind, henchmen, villains, a scheme, and heroes.  So many combos here that I think it would be difficult to repeat one - especially if you get the Dark City expansion that effectively doubles your cards.

Bottom line - a game that plays relatively quickly that has an attractive theme and art with lots of variation.  It is straightforward enough for kids to be able to play but has enough twists and turns to keep me entertained as well.

RATING: 9
Deck builders are probably my favorite type of game, and Legendary is an excellent one.  The sheer volume of expansions (see below) mean it will take a long time to run out of material.  

This takes the Ascension model of deck building (a central row of cards to buy, instead of the Dominion set stacks) and adds a separate row for villains to defeat.  One of my problems with Ascension (which I have only played the app) is that sometimes you will build a combat deck expecting monsters to come out, but very few monsters do.  Legendary fixes this by having two separate purchase rows, one for adding cards to your deck and one for removing threats.

My only real complaint is the tallying up of points at the end of the game.  I love cooperative games, and this game is an amazing one.  Tacking on a competitive element at the very end of the game just to have a singular winner was a misstep.  I don't even teach that part of the game anymore.  Unfortunately this makes some heroes like Black Widow less useful, though the addition of new bystanders with special abilities in subsequent sets ameliorates this slightly.

RATING: 8.5
I own this game for several months now and I think this game is really awesome. At first I gave this game a solid 7, but several months later I still play the game a lot, and for that alone I think it’s worth a 8.5. With most of my games I loose interest after playing it a dozen times. I play this game at least once in two weeks and it is still great fun. The reason for this are the smart game mechanics. You choose the Mastermind you would like to battle and which heroes you would like to use for that. There are also different “schemes” that makes the game more unpredictable. With the different combination of schemes, heroes and masterminds you’ll have huge different variations of the game. 

The only reason why it is not a 9 or 10 is the artwork. The game comes with several heroes and for every hero there are several different type of cards that you can play. Instead of making a new artwork for every different type of card, the creators used one artwork for all the cards for one hero. With the Dark City expansion they got clever and every card had his own artwork. The artwork itself is beautiful and gives a great look and feel for the game. The (lack of) artwork on the game board is a bit boring. They should have made it a bit more exciting.

RATING: 7.2
My initial reaction to this game was that it was a lot of fun. I enjoyed my first couple plays a lot. The variability of the interacting schemes, masterminds, and villains promises a lot of replay-ability and seemed to insure that each game would feel a little different.

After playing this a few times, though, I'm starting to see some interesting flow issues arise. Some hero/ villain/ mastermind/ scheme combos make this feel very fast paced and smooth. Others can stall the game quite a bit. Just picking random heroes seems like a very bad idea... they really need to play off of each other. You can get bad combos in other deck building games as well, but the effect a bad combo can have on this game can make it quite tedious and pretty much unplayable.

There also seems to be a bit of a runaway leader issue in this game. I think this is actually a side effect to one of the things I really liked about this game: there is a separate victory point pile, so that victory points don't clog up your deck. 

I also get a bit of the Ascension blues with this game. I dislike having such a limited choice on what I can buy on my turn. Five heroes choices just isn't enough, especially if/when you get several high costing heroes clogging up the works early in the game. I wish there was a way to clear out the options and draw five new cards at the start of your turn.

Overall it's a pretty nice system, but with some issues. And you have to be a little more thoughtful when setting up the card selection at the beginning of the game than you do with some other deck builders.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.1
Solo Player Value = Excellent. This is fun to play solo, but just a little better with more.

Two Player Value = Excellent

Three Player Value = Excellent


Legendary is truly fun to play. As of this writing, April 16, 2014, Legendary is my favorite deck pooling game.

Legendary is a cooperative deck pooling game where the players play as super heroes trying to stop a Mastermind villain before he can fulfill his evil plan.

While I am not always big on theme, I think theme is the best place to start for Legendary. Not only is the game packed with theme, the theme is wonderfully worked into every aspect of the game. The theme is very integral to the game and fits the mechanics fantastically. I think the theme is a large part of what makes the game so much fun to play. Playing as a super hero is just fun.

Also of note is the great artwork on the cards. The artwork gives players a great feeling of being in a comic book. It is really well done.

The players must work together to fight against the game, the Mastermind villain. Each turn the player acts as the bad guy, then he gets his own set of actions to fight against the bad guy.

The deck pooling mechanic is handled nicely. By now I am sure every gamer knows and understands the Dominion deck pooling mechanic. Legendary offers nothing new this the tried and true mechanic, but it does work very well.

Legendary does offer a new and rather ingenious system for stacking combinations. It is this system that helps make the game so much fun to play. The heroes each have a certain type and an affiliation. These types and affiliations work together to form chains that stack into combinations. Playing multiple heroes of a given type and/or affiliation combine together to form bigger bonuses and attacks. It is these stacking combos that make the game a treat to play. Choosing the right heroes for your deck to continue your chain of combos is an important part of the game.

The actions of the Mastermind villain is handled randomly by using a deck of cards built just for him. I think this works very well and gives an element of suspense to the game.

Legendary has extreme replayability. Each game is governed by a plot the Mastermind is trying to accomplish. There are many different plots to play through. I find this a great way to keep the game fresh.

Additionally, the difficulty of the game is extremely flexible. The heroes you choose have a huge impact on the games difficulty. You can directly effect the game difficulty by the choice heroes. This is great way to scale the game down for new players or ramp it up for experienced players.

Legendary scales extremely well from being a solo game to holding several players. This is mostly due to the fact that the game is essentially a multi-player solitaire game. Each player acts independently, yet all players must work together to defeat the Mastermind.

This multi-player solitaire design becomes overly complicated with the addition of a competitive element. While all players must work together, each player is also competing against each other to see who can fight the Mastermind most. I really do not like this cooperative/competitive design. I strongly believe a game should be either cooperative or competitive, but not both. When I play I make the game a completely cooperative game and totally eliminate the competitive aspects. The game works better this way.

I can say that the set-up time for the game can be severe. The players will have a deck of heroes to build decks from. The Mastermind will also have a deck to draw cards from and run the game. Both of these decks will need to be set-up prior to playing and does take some time. This could turn people away from the game.


Pros - 
- Easy to learn
- Great theme that works very well
- Great Art
- Extreme replayability 
- Easily changeable difficulty


Cons -
- Long set-up time
- I do not like the cooperative yet competitive mechanic
- Some people simply don't like super heroes


Overall Playability = 7.6

Design = 7
Strategy = 8
Luck = 9
Artwork & Components = 8
Use of Mechanics = 8
Time of Play = 7
Fun = 8
Innovation = 6
Analysis Paralysis = 8
Theme = 8

***This game is scored including the expansions


[b]-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------[/b]


Here I will discuss the Legendary expansion [thing=137762][/thing].

The first expansion for Legendary adds a lot to the base game.  In fact, it literally doubles the size of the base game.  Twice as many heroes are now available.  Twice as many Masterminds with twice as many plots are now available.  This goes a long way to increase the games replayability even further.  

The new heroes have new abilities that trigger with the proper stacking of types and affiliations in combinations.  The new abilities are fun and help the players in the struggle against evil.

The new Masterminds are now more powerful as well and bring their own new abilities to the fight.  A few new Masterminds are truly deadly.

The new plot Schemes are fun and offer some really well thought out challenges for the players.

In Dark City the artwork is not really improved from the base game, but it is enhanced a bit.  By that I mean that each hero no longer has a single picture representing all his cards.  Now each hero has three or four different pictures.  Each picture represents the different abilities of that hero.  I like the new artwork as it helps differentiate the various abilities and skills each hero has.

Other than the new heroes, Masterminds and plots mentioned above, this expansion changes nothing from the base game.  The same mechanics and rules set are used.  This expansion does not alter the game in any way.  It simply adds to it.  I think that is good thing since the base game is well designed.

While this expansion does not change the base game, it does add enough new content to make me want to reevaluate my scores.


Overall Playability = 8.1

Design = 8
Strategy = 8
Luck = 9
Artwork & Components = 9
Use of Mechanics = 8
Time of Play = 7
Fun = 9
Innovation = 7
Analysis Paralysis = 8
Theme = 8


[b]-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------[/b]


Here I will discuss the Legendary expansion [thing=142020][/thing].

This expansion is much smaller than the previous expansion.  Fantastic 4 brings 100 new cards to the game in the form of 5 new heroes, 2 new Masterminds and villains and a few new plot schemes.

As stated by the name, this expansion deals only with the addition of the Fantastic 4 hero group to the base game.  Everything in this expansion is based around the Fantastic 4 hero group.

The new heroes are all the members of the Fantastic 4.  The new Masterminds and villains are the natural enemies of the Fantastic 4.  The new plot Schemes are all in line with events from the Fantastic 4 story.

The new heroes offer the players a few new special powers to aid you in the fight.  These, of course, are offset by the new powers the of Mastermind and villains.  

I very much like that this expansion is small and set toward the one hero group.  With only the single hero group being used, you can completely make the game about that one hero group.  By using only the cards in this expansion, everything in the game totally surrounds, and becomes about, the Fantastic 4.  This gives the player a great feeling of immersion and truly brings out the flavor of the game.

Once again, this expansion does not change the base game in any way.  It simply adds to it.  This still works for me as the original design works so well.

I do enjoy the new additions this expansion brings.  However, I do not think it offers enough to alter my scoring of the game.  Therefore, the game carry the score when this expansion is included.


[b]-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------[/b]


Here I will discuss the Legendary expansion [thing=149922][/thing].

This write-up might look like a direct copy of the one above.  That is because it is.  At this point the expansions are fairly pre-set.  Simply replace all instance of one hero group with another hero group and the expansions are identical.  I see this as a good thing.  The base is so much fun to play, that changing it would be bad.  By just adding the new heroes and villains the game takes on their feeling yet stays the same.
  

This expansion is much smaller than the previous expansion. Paint the Town Red brings 100 new cards to the game in the form of 5 new heroes, 2 new Masterminds and villains and a few new plot schemes.

As stated by the name, this expansion deals only with the addition of the Spider Man hero group to the base game. Everything in this expansion is based around the Spider Man hero group.

The new heroes are all the members of the Spider Man. The new Masterminds and villains are the natural enemies of Spider Man. The new plot Schemes are all in line with events from the Spider Man story.

The new heroes offer the players a few new special powers to aid you in the fight. These, of course, are offset by the new powers the of Mastermind and villains. 

I very much like that this expansion is small and set toward the one hero group. With only the single hero group being used, you can completely make the game about that one hero group. By using only the cards in this expansion, everything in the game totally surrounds, and becomes about, Spider Man. This gives the player a great feeling of immersion and truly brings out the flavor of the game.

Once again, this expansion does not change the base game in any way. It simply adds to it. This still works for me as the original design works so well.

I do enjoy the new additions this expansion brings. However, I do not think it offers enough to alter my scoring of the game. Therefore, the game carry the score when this expansion is included.


[b]-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------[/b]


Here I will discuss the Legendary expansion [thing=163106][/thing].

As with the other Legendary expansions, this will look very familiar due to the small box expansion are all following the same blueprint.  But I really think that is a bonus.  The small box expansions allow the game to fully take on the flavor of a given hero group.

This expansion is centered around the Guardians of the Galaxy.

The new pieces are the same.  5 Heroes, 2 Villain groups, 2 Masterminds and 4 new Schemes.

This expansion also brings in a new mechanic by using Shards and Artifacts. 

Shards are collectible items that subsidize Attack when used.  But it is tricky because both Heroes, Villains and Masterminds can gain and use Shards.   Using the Shards is fun new addition and a big tool in fighting evil.

Artifacts are really just Heroes or Villains that stay in play and give a bonus or usable power each turn.  This is also a fun new addition to the mechanics and brings with it a small level of tableau building.

Overall, this is a fun new expansion and brings two good new mechanics to the game.

RATING: 8
I've had this game for a while now, but haven't played it a lot in the last couple of months. Making it part of my 10x10 challenge helped me get back in to it. The only really bad things I have to say about it is that setup and tear down takes a while. I'm also struggling to fit all the (sleeved) cards in the base box, but others have managed it, so I probably just need to rethink how I put them away.

The game itself is fun. At times a walk in the park, at times nigh impossible to beat. I mostly play it solo, but when introducing it to new people, it takes minutes to explain, a couple of rounds to play and everyone's usually on board with what's going on. In itself, it's a basic deck builder with a Marvel theme and Marvel art. You'll probably either like it or you won't.

I'll probably play this any time someone asks, unless there's a time constraint or there's something else I really want to try out first.

RATING: 6
Thematically, maybe the first box should have been The Avengers vs. their archrivals, rather than the most popular Marvel heroes vs. the most popular Marvel villains. Because it felt rather disjointed that The Hulk and Deadpool were fighting Dr. Doom. Bwuh? Also, you recruit heroes with SHIELD agents. Which never happened in the comics. Other than that, each hero has a different way of play, which I think is great. Some cards from different heroes synergize with each other, adding to the uniqueness of each combination of heroes! 

*****

I still don't get what my deck represents. If I'm playing solo, it's a team of superheroes taking potshots at villains. Okay, that makes sense. But if I'm playing cooperatively, and your deck and my deck have the same superhero card, then what? Does that mean Hawkeye is jumping around between  our groups shooting arrows and stuff? And why is Dr. Doom hiring the Brotherhood of Mutants and using Sentinels? I don't remember him doing that in comics. And why SHIELD agents? I think with the Ultimate universe and movies SHIELD agents recruited superheroes, but in most comics story arcs, the superheroes acted on their own. The mechanics are just fine, but they really don't fit the mechanics well (cf. Dicemasters).

RATING: 9
I have seen the light - this game really is a solid challenger to DOminin in my estimation. Incorporates elements of Nightfall and Ascension - both of which I personally pretty much loathe - into the deck management and point chasing of Dominion. Loads of interesting interactions in this game - like the way you can have a feel for the strategies available in a given set up by the types of cards expected in each heroes cards - but no guarantee that the killer combos will end up in your hand. Really, really good as a competitive game, plenty of opportunities in most set ups to spite your 'allies'. The master villain is such a great take on the Province Deck - victory points sitting outside your deck make decks generally more fun to play and less prone to choking, but there's still plenty of challenge in building a good deck. I think that people might have a bit less fun playing this purely cooperatively - would get too repetitive, be too long, and too easy - but maybe I am too competitive to appreciate that. Great design. The Punisher thinning out the Shield Agents in your deck being thematically explained as exterminating bent cops is one of the delightful little details.
